--- 帖子 #1 ---
Hi all and welcome to the DAILY95PIPS strategy.

Before we start I urge you to paper trade any new strategy including this one before committing any of your own funds. Thorough testing is crucial before taking any strategy live.

Also bear in mind that this system is by no means new and may look familiar to some of you. I am simply passing it on from my predecessors/mentors in the hope that it adds to your existing trading arsenal and increases your trading results.

The basis of this system is VERY simple and has proven to be profitable, though I am adjusting the money management/profit targets. So results for this revised version will be realised on this thread. I must also emphasise the well known phrase that "past performance is no guarantee of future returns".

I will add the daily trading results to this thread as we go along. See post#1602 for updated results for the current week. Weekly and individual pairs results are at post #1602. Monthly totals are at post#1602. (Please disregard the next post #2 as I am unable to add to it.)

That being said, let us proceed with the strategy.

OVERVIEW:

This is a pure "set and forget" system where trades are placed at the same time everyday. The option is also there for those inclined to monitor their positions to adjust stop levels as profit targets are reached. Please note that there is currently an Expert Advisor being developed that automates the trading of this strategy, thus keeping to the set and forget objective. Please click on the paperclip at the top right hand side of the page to find the current versions. For those new to using Expert Advisors you will need a broker that uses an MT4 platform such as North Finance, IBFX, ODL, FXDD to name a few. For instruction on installing EA's go to: http://www.halcyonfx.com/howtoinstall.htm

By setting multiple profit targets we are exercising money management, while aiming for 95pips profit from a 50pip move in price.

We will simply be placing orders 5pips above the previous days HIGH and 5pips below the previous days LOW.(Actually, it's more like the previous 17hrs at 5pm EST.)

Use a 30pip stop loss for all orders.

Orders are placed on Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday, Thursday and Friday.

EXECUTION:

1.) At 5pm EST open the 1hr chart (2hrs b4 start of the Asian session) of USDJPY. ( In an attempt to pre-empt questions about how this strategy works on other pairs, I will post results comparing GBPUSD, GBPJPY, EURJPY, and EURUSD. You're welcome to add to the list.)

For those who need help with converting timezones go to: http://www.timeanddate.com/worldclock/converter.html

For those whose brokers spreads are still wide at 5pm EST on Sunday (which is 7am my time on a Monday here in Brisbane), in order to avoid the wide spreads you may need to wait until they reduce to normal before placing the orders for the day. I typically have to wait until around 8pm EST for Oanda's spreads to reduce back to normal.

2.) Use the high and low of the previous 17hrs. For Mondays orders go back as far as 00:00 EST on Friday for high and low.

3.) Open a total of 6 PENDING orders (for each pair) including 3 BUY STOPS and 3 SELL STOPS that expire within 24hrs (I use 18hrs) as follows:

Buy/Long Orders:

i. #1 - Entry = HIGH+5pips, Take Profit=15pips, S/L=30pips

ii. #2 - Entry = HIGH+5pips, Take Profit=30pips, S/L=30pips

iii. #3 - Entry = HIGH+5pips, Take Profit=50pips, S/L=30pips

Sell/Short Orders:

i. #1 - Entry = LOW-5pips, Take Profit=15pips, S/L=30pips

ii. #2 - Entry = LOW-5pips, Take Profit=30pips, S/L=30pips

iii. #3 - Entry = LOW-5pips, Take Profit=50pips, S/L=30pips

That's it.

Once you have placed your orders you are free to go and do something else with your day as this strategy does not require you to be monitoring the trades. Though, as already mentioned, to maximise results you may choose to adjust stop levels when profit targets are reached which by the way is automatically done by the EA.

There can be 4 possible outcomes after either the long or short trades are triggered:

1.) All 3 profit targets are reached for a total of +95pips.

2.) The first 2 profit targets are reached (+45pips) and the remaining lot is stopped out (-30pips) leaving a total of +15pips.

3.) The first profit target is reached (+15pips) and the two remaining lots are stopped out for a total of -45pips.

4.) All 3 lots are stopped out for a total of -90pips.

Additional to this is the variable outcomes of when both the long and short trades are triggered.

Also note that for those so inclined to monitor the trades, stop levels may be adjusted on remaining lot/s to protect already achieved profits. Trailing stops may also be used at your discretion. These features are included in the EA.

Please note that as a general rule of thumb you should not risk any more than 3% of your trading account on any one trade.

Therefore, with the DAILY95PIPS strategy the order size will need to be divided between the long and short orders. The total potential loss on the long orders (90pips) will therefore add up to 3% of your trading account.

Alternatively, you could risk 3% of your trading capital on EACH order, totalling 9% of your trading capital being risked for the long trades. The same applies to the short orders.

Happy trading everyone !

--- 帖子 #15 ---
Yes Joe, this is a VERY mechanical system...the advantage of this is that 99.9% of emotion can be removed from the trading process, and that's the great thing about a set and forget strategy.

In terms of past results, I have seen versions of this strategy that aim for profits of 60pips from a 30pip move in price, risking 90pips. The average monthly result is approx. 300pips.

The basis of this system is the same ie. placing limit orders 5pips above and below the previous days high and low, however I have introduced a variation on the money management strategy which involves aiming for 95pips while risking 90pips. Therefore, I do not have any historical results to share with you at this point in time...sorry 'bout that. The results of this new approach are being forward tested and posted on this thread.

I hope this doesn't confuse anyone.

--- 帖子 #77 ---
just found this thread.. i am a big fan of mechanical systems and although this is a very simplistic method it has enough merit to warrent further exploration!

i think the long term expectancy of such a system can be greatly increased through the following:

1.

trades are taken only on "inside days"

or

since inside days are few and far between perhaps increasing risk or doubling trade size on such days

2.

apply some sort of martingale or similar compounding technique to losing days

ie - after one losing day increase bet on 2nd day

or

following a winning day decrease position size for next day

obviously in order to effeciently fine tune the money management aspect one would need and expert written as manual backtesting would take hours if not days, maybe if there are no other takers i will donate one when time allows

GL

- Derek

--- 帖子 #78 ---
What do you mean my "inside days"?

thanks

--- 帖子 #79 ---
an inside day is one in which neither the high or low of the previous day was exceeded (for exampe if the highs and lows of today were inside the range of the previous day)

as opposed to an "outside day" in which both the high and low of the previous day is exceeded

GL

--- 帖子 #105 ---
Hi,

isn't this in effect identical to the systems proposed by Tkimble? (check under threads started by that user after checking his username"). >>> http://forexfactory.com/member.php?u=25926

I'd like to point out that by using 90 pips stop and 95 pips TP you are effectively getting around 1:1 risk/reward, i.e. need a chance of MORE than 50% to end up profitable in a simplified "all or nothing scenario".

How it boils down with the partials I don't know, but assuming that no stops are moved at any point, chance shouldn't change much...not that I know the advanced stochastic/statistic part of all this. All I see is 3x30=90 at risk, 15+30+50=95 possible to gain.

This may or not work in the long run, but it requires insane patience, dedication and faith that it will work in the first place, as witnessed by the dying out of the tkimble threads once the strong trending periods which are needed for profitability also died down again..

Just wanted to point out to be careful with anything that has only 1:1 risk/reward and to be SURE that it's something that arguably works due to certain reasons.

And to mention tkimble's stuff, since those threads might hold some interesting stuff as well.(for additional ideas or similiar e.g.)

No offense

Take care,

SeekingLight

--- 帖子 #107 ---
Hi Hans.

Let us be clear as to what the 18hrs expiry is referring to here.

When you place the pending/limit orders, depending on your broker, there is usually an option to select a time expiry for those limit orders. I have chosen to use 18hrs to try to avoid having a trade triggered just before I'm due to place new orders for the next day.

To simplify your calculations for the high and low, open a 1 hour chart at 5pm ESTand take the high and low of that day (again, depending on your broker, the new daily candle may not have been opened ).

I hope this helps.

mike

--- 帖子 #109 ---
Hi SeekingLight.

Yes, the BASIS of this strategy is very similar to some of tkimble's (which I am quite familiar with) though definitely NOT identical.

In fact, I have tried his weeklyscalping system and am currently paper trading his SAR system. He also has a dailyscalping strategy which he uses in conjunction with the weekly. Both rely on the probability of breakouts using the previous day or weeks' close, though with a few more variables to consider.

I haven't continued with the weekly system as the trades are often stopped out before the weekly trend is established...so re-entry can occur  multiple times (thus increased  drawdown) before the trades are profitable for the week. Personally I was not comfortable with this experience. However, overall, coupled with good money management, this strategy seems quite sound.

In a very simplified sense the risk:reward for Daily95pips is approx. 1:1. We also need to consider the 4+ possible scenarios as described in post#1.

One very important key to successful trading is indeed PATIENCE. It is the 'need for speed' that all too often has many a trader crushed in their early days of learning how to be a successful trader. As long as the strategy and money management systems are sound, the rest is simply implementation which actually just becomes a seemingly boring routine, especially with a system as simple as Daily95pips.

Also bear in mind that the very purpose of this thread is to simultaneously share and test this strategy to ascertain it's feasability.

cheers

mike

Quer1234,

I think you and Mike may not be trading on exactly the same time frame. Each broker delivers charts whose day begins at a unique world time, i.e., GMT +1, GMT -2, etc., so unless you are using the exact same start and end times as Mike, you may experience some discrepancies, especially

with a pair like EU/JY, which can easily move 50-70 pips or more in any given hour.

--- 帖子 #116 ---
Hi lads.

In an attempt to clarify the above, I can only share with you how I have the timeframe set up for my own trading:

1.) I have the clock on my computer set at EST.

2.) My broker is Oanda, and the time on my trading platform is the same as my computer.

3.) At 5pm EST I open the daily chart and take the high and low of the current daily candle (I may have to remove from post#1 the part about waiting for the new daily candle to open, though again it depends on your broker and timeframe ). The exception will be on Monday when I take the high and low from the previous Friday, unless there has been significant activity over the weekend in which case I may take Sundays data.

The main point to consider is that based on different timeframes there will be different results. Somedays others will get a better result than I and visa versa. This happened in the first day ( checkout the first few posts) where some of the guys on this thread got +95pips on one of the pairs

(I can't recall which one) when I got only +15pips.

We can still see that overall my results have been good.

Once settling on your own approach to this strategy, the idea is to just stick to it and if the results are good you know you're onto a winner.

I hope this helps you all.

mike

--- 帖子 #117 ---
Hi Mike,

Thanks for clarifying.

I also felt that it really made no difference when you ended your day, as long as you were consistent about it (though I have not tested this theory as yet).

But just to clarify further:

Your high for 8/30 only included the time from 0000 - 1700 EST. You did not go back a full 24 hours (to 8/29 at 1700), and therefore the  earlier higher highs that occurred around 24 hours earlier did not play into the picture, so your [high+5 pip] target entry came sooner at a LOWER price than if you had included those earlier highs of the day. That, my friend, is why you made +95 while another trader lost -90. Problem solved!

Please correct me if I'm wrong here.

Thanks so much!

--- 帖子 #126 ---
Hi TheThing.

I'm demo trading this strategy with the purpose of shortlisting the pairs I am currently using on this thread to 3-4. I'll then continue demo trading these remaining pairs until it is clear that they are consistently profitable. I'll then go live, using a money management system whereby 3% of trading capital will be risked on each pair's trade for the day, so that if there are 4 pairs remaining, a maximum of 12% of my trading account will be at risk each day if we diligently cancel the short orders if the long orders are triggered and visa versa. If there are only 3 pairs it will be 9%. The purpose of using this strategy on multiple pairs is for diversification and spreading of risk. Therefore, risking up to 12% each day may turn out to be quite comfortable.

mike

--- 帖子 #130 ---
I'm glad to be of assistance Jeff.

I must say that you are a brave man for going live on this strategy(if that's what you meant by "trading $1 lots" ) this early in the piece.

I was actually a bit late to place the demo orders today, and came back later to find that some would've already triggered. What I see so far is that the GBPJPY long has ended with +15pips. As I am currently paper trading this strategy, I can look back over the charts and see the likely results (unless price came perilously close to TP or SL in which case I usually give the conservative outcome the benefit of the doubt).

I try not to get too emotionally caught up in the trades and as a result make decisions before the trades have run their course. That's the very reason I am inclined towards set and forget strategies such as this. Try to bear in mind that there is always the chance of a trade coming back and reaching full profit....and if it doesn't and goes the other way, so be it. That indicates to me that the system may need a little more tweaking to maximise performance without me interferring with the trades themselves. For example, so far we've seen that EURGBP is potentially not as suited to this strategy as other pairs. So, we may just need to remove it from the list.

That being said, I'll admit that I still can't resist checking on the trades throughout the day. And in those times when I see the price is just near the take profit level and I feel the urge to close out and protect profits, I force myself to walk away and come back later because I can feel my emotions being overly drawn into the trading process, and that's what I want to avoid.

I just know from experience that the more room there is to make desicions after trades have been placed, the more chance there is of being taken on an emotional rollercoaster. I'm trying to streamline my trading so that this doesn't occur.

As I've heard it said: "trading is 20% skills and 80% psychology", so it's the psychology part that we are addressing here.

Regarding ascertaining your results with Oanda; if you have physically placed either demo or live trades with the 3 profit targets as per this system, whenever a profit target is hit a green dot will appear on your chart. If you are stopped out, a red dot will appear. So, depending on how many green dots appear, you can easily calculate the result in pips:

3 green dots = +95pips

2 green dots & 1 red dot = +15pips

1 green dot  &  1 red dot  =  -45pips

1 red dot = -90pips

Alternatively, simply check the movement of price from your entry levels eg. if long entry on GBPUSD is 2.0196 and price goes past 2.0246 you will know that you've achieved all 3 profit targets for a total of +95pips.

mike

--- 帖子 #140 ---
firstly mate the date your asking is 08/31

now the range on 08/30 was 219 pips the high was 158.96 and the low was 156.77 so the 10% of the range is 21.9 round it to 22 pips so your entry points for the next day will be previous day's high minus 22 pips for going short and for going long your entry point for the next day will be previous day's low plus 22 pips.

To go short 158.96-22 pips = 158.74

To go long 156.77+22 pips = 156.99

Finally remember your day is supposed to start at 17:00 Et and end at 17:00 Et.

--- 帖子 #150 ---
Hi Bksujal,

Please correct me if I'm wrong, but it appears that your strategy is the opposite of Mikelath's "Daily 95 Pips" system.

He goes long on the previous day's high, plus 5 pips. However, you go short on the previous day's high, less 10% of the day's range.

He goes short on the previous day's low, less 5 pips. However, you go long on the previous day's low, plus 10% of thd day's range.

In summary, it seems that your strategy is a retracement strategy, while Mikelath's strategy is a trending strategy. Perhaps there's a way to blend the best of the two strategies. Any suggestions...

What are your SL & TP for a given currency pair (I believe you mentioned that your r/r is 1:2)?

Also, wouldn't it be better to not factor in the 10% of ATR?  It seems that by including thiis item you increase the risk...

Thanks,

Walt

My idea is to do this. We got the high and low of the previous day.

So as per the rules of Daily95pips I go long high+5 pips and go short high -10% of the previous days high-low. The SL of the long is the short leg. We could do on another account or if hedging available on the same account the reverse. Or if the previous bar is bullish just do the long/short leg. if the previous bar is bearish than do the short/long leg. But this is a completely different strategy and would require another thread.

--- 帖子 #161 ---
Well, that was fun!

Last night I traded eu/us, eu/jy, eus/jy, for real money, @ $1/pip. I ended up losing around -60 pips, but I learned quite a bit. What I learned was that the 30 pip SL was too deep for my style, and that a 50 pip TP is a bit too ambitious. Again, for my style. That's not to say it won't work for others, but while watching my trades unfold today, I saw some clear profits turn back because I sensed my TP points were too high.

So, tonight, I've decided to tweak things a bit, to make my expectations a bit more modest and - hopefully - keep my losses lower. Here's my plan:

Same entry, same time frame, H+5, L-5.

SL = 15

TP: 10, 15, 20

It's possible I'll get stopped out everywhere, but I've cut my potential losses in half, so we'll have to see how it all plays out.

I might miss a big move with a 50 pip gain, but normally I am at the computer, so I would be able to move my TP in that case (unfortunately, I will be out most of the day tomorrow, so I'll have no idea what's happening until I return).

It's just an experiment, a tweak of what looks like a terrific system from Mikelath. I may go back to the original, but will report on my results later tomorrow. Mike said earlier that this was not just an offering of a system, but an attempt to tweak it. So, I'll do my part, with 1$ lots. Another poster said it: I just find it impossible to demo-trade seriously, and am much more involved when I have some real money at stake.

I definitely think entry is key here. If we have it right, good money management will let us win.

Another thing I learned is that, having been scalping mostly, I really like to see all those double-digit pips on the board. It's definitely more fun to play with bigger numbers.

Any comments or suggestions?

Ok guys have a look at this chart for eur/jpy which i used today I must tell this is one of my most favourite pairs.

We would be looking to go long because the day ended close to the low's so more chances of a long trade than a shorter one. 2. move your SL to BE using whatever rules you belive is valid. For example when the second TP has been hit.. This way you will not turn winners to loosers.

--- 帖子 #191 ---
I'd just like to thank everyone for their contribution to this thread. The great thing about forexfactory is that there are so many experienced traders to help newbies like myself learn more about trading.

Some of the things I've learnt so far from this thread are:

1.) This strategy is suited to a trending market, NOT a ranging market. How we identify them before they occur is another story....hindsight is certainly a wonderful thing.

2.) Moving up the stop loss on the 50TP trade can help to maximise profits.

According to the profit targets on post#1, this can mean the difference between gaining +15pips and +45pips. This however, relies on being around to monitor the trades and adjust the stops accordingly, which takes away from the original 'set and forget' objective.

This thread is proving to be a great learning tool.

mike:

--- 帖子 #192 ---
One of the problems with using a system like this over a wide range of different pairs, is the differences in volatility. I think that instead of using arbitrary figures for taking profit and for stops, perhaps you should consider using a percentage of ATR. For example for the take profit levels, you could use 10%, 20% and 30% of ATR for each pair, with a stop of say 20% ATR (I haven't tested any of these, they are just numbers off the top of my head). I also agree with Bullrock, that you need to have a position that gets held till the end of day, or perhaps 2X ATR or something so you can pick up those occasional big moves that happen only a few days each month, as those often news driven events will probably account for the majority of your monthly profit IMHO.

Axel.

--- 帖子 #193 ---
I have traded forex for some time now and most often I trade breakouts,so I will add my 2 cents. I like the basic thought of the point for the breakout,however I have yet to find a generic set it and forget it system.

1. Time of day is very important,I believe placing Oder's at 5PM is asking for trouble,especially if we do not close mid range on the daily candle. Any pair that deals with the jpy that is close to triggering,will often sweep the trigger and fail. The first 1 to 2 hours of the Asian session can be some of the most difficult forex action of the entire 24 hour period,imo. The closer orders can be entered to the open of the EUR...GBP session,greatly raises the probability that the breakout will have follow thru.

2. In my mind the whole basis of the trade is assuming you are going to get 50 pips,that is a very big assumption. Any time you fail to reach the 50 pip level and it comes back to stop you out the best you can have is a 15 pip winner. I have used a trailing stop on the last third of each of my entries. This change alone has greatly reduced my losses.

3. Failed breakouts are most often nasty!!! in many of the pairs it is not necessary to hang around for 30 pips if the level is broken and then quickly fails. When I look to enter a trade one of the most important aspects in my decision making is where can I find a key level to hide behind in terms of a stop. I may find a real nice entry point,but if the level I need to hide behind is too far away I will most often pass on the trade or use much smaller size.

4.In the same manner assuming you are long and i will use the Eur/Usd as my example tonight. Previous day high is 3710 where do I expect the next key resistance level that will slow this play down. The next key level is R1 at 3722. The same thinking applies as when looking for a stop point. Where is my first target,and in this case it is R1 and that is only 7 pips away if you place your entry 5 pips beyond the previous day high. Therefore, I can not enter this trade because I do not have 30 pips between key levels to get my partial. In this case I don't even have room for the 15 partial. In my mind the Eur/usd is not even a consideration on the long side in this session.

5.Lets now review the Eur/Usd short entry.Previous day low is 3635.You already have to break below S1 3647 to get to your trigger.This is very important for two reasons. First the eur/usd often uses s1 and r1 as stopping points,maybe even moreso than many of the other pairs. Your entry now becomes 3630( which is too great of a distance on this pair in my mind),and you now Identify you next key level which is s2 at 3603!! BIngo you now have the parameters you are looking for. Well almost and this is extremely important!!!! your target on this play should be your normal 15 pips on the first entry but your second target should be like 25 or 26 pips......not just your standard 30 pips. S2 3603 is a very key level but that does not mean it will always hit that number exact,you dont want to screw up a play trying to get to the exact pip,nor would you ever want your second partial a few pips beyond s2,it may never break thru that level. Ok now lets not forget about our stop price just incase yhis beautiful setup fails. Remember we had to break thru S1 3647 to get to the trigger . If we make a new low and then come back and test s1 and we can not hold that level to the downside,there is no longer a reason to stay with this trade. My stop would then be 3650, 3 pips above S1. In the event I get stopped out my exposure is only 20 pips,and I will bet that if s1 does not hold your 30 pip stop also gets taken out. Very long winded but a different way possibly to view the setups,no two setups are usually the same!

--- 帖子 #194 ---
The more I analyze it, the more Bksujal's system of range trading makes sense.  The market ranges more than it trends, especially with cross currencies.  However, to protect against a trending market with a ranging system it may be feasible to take the current price as of 00:00 GMT and add 25% of the prior day's range to determine your short position.  Subtract 25% of the prior day's range to determine your long position.  Set TP at intervals of 10, 15, 20, & 25 pips from entry price.  I would set the SL at 50 pips from entry price.  The key is to not trade during major news events.  I would focus on traditional range bound pairs such as EUR/CHF, EUR/GBP, or perhaps even EUR/JPY.  I think this could yield 25 - 60 pips daily with minimal chance of a SL.

Thanks,

Walt

A bit of this and that.

So I have made a bit of analysis in excel.

There can be problem with the accuracy because I have done the analysis on daily data. The analysis takes into consideration only the long side.
The strategy:

5 units -> 4 TP + 1 EOD

TP1 15% of the daily ATR(14)

TP1 30% of the daily ATR(14)

TP1 45% of the daily ATR(14)

TP1 60% of the daily ATR(14)

SL is 20% of the daily ATR(14)

The analysis:

Gu from 1999.09.14 - 2007.08.31 or 2073 days

Only long side. (I was lazy  )

Total:

TP1 = 15 890.7 pips

TP2 = 22 101.8 pips

TP3 = 22 381.7 pips

TP4 = 20 614.1 pips

EOD = 41 633 pips
Total = 122 621.2 pips without the losses

Losses without break even and without sl that is close at the end of the day: -298 918 pips
Result: -176 296 pips or -85 pips a day.

Clearly this way it is a looser strategy.

Losses with moving to be after TP2 is hit: -112 214 pips
Result: +10407.2 pips or 5 pips a day or 1 pip a day / unit

It is better but this is still something I wouldn't go for.

Now let us see the effect of 20% of SL of the ATR(14) and move to BE when TP2 is hit: -26 402.8 pips
Result: +96 209.4 pips or 46 pips a day or 9.2 pip a day / unit

Well this is not too bad.

Have fun.

Regards

bullrock

--- 帖子 #211 ---
Although it's always a good idea to speak with your broker when you're having problems, I don't think broker restrictions is the problem here. No broker will stop you from placing trades where your TP or SL is 25 pips or more. Doesn't make sense. One thing to double-check is that your order expiry date is actually set for some period in the future.

It's also possible that your account is not set up properly in the first place, or some files have become corrupted within your software. If this is the case, I suspect you would be unable to enter ANY trade at all!

Can you enter a regular market order (instant execution)? If not, I would re-run your setup program (MQ4setup.exe or something similar), and when it asks you if you are willing to receive your broker's newsletters, you must say "yes." Then, try it again, and if it still doesn't work, contact your broker and report the problem.

Let us know how you make out.

Hope that helps...

[quote=mikelath;1559420]Hi all and welcome to the DAILY95PIPS strategy.

Buy/Long Orders:

i. #1 - Entry = HIGH+5pips, Take Profit=15pips, S/L=30pips

ii. #2 - Entry = HIGH+5pips, Take Profit=30pips, S/L=30pips

iii. #3 - Entry = HIGH+5pips, Take Profit=50pips, S/L=30pips

Sell/Short Orders:

i. #1 - Entry = LOW-5pips, Take Profit=15pips, S/L=30pips

ii. #2 - Entry = LOW-5pips, Take Profit=30pips, S/L=30pips

iii. #3 - Entry = LOW-5pips, Take Profit=50pips, S/L=30pips

hi sameer.

Good question.

To simplify, in post#1 I've suggested using the previous 17 hrs of data at 5pmEST.However, Monday is a different story, and I'll need to edit post#1 in this regard.

Today I've realised that firstly the above approach is not really applicable on Monday's. Using Friday's data would be the simplest. That being said, we need to consider that sometimes there is significant activity over the weekend, and that sometimes price has already broken above or below the previous days high or low.

I'm also finding that my broker ( Oanda ) has wide spreads at the time I usually place the orders for Monday. So, I need to wait until the spreads reduce first.

So yes, we need to adjust for Monday's trading.

Personally, I am using the previous 17hrs from when I'm due to place the orders(when the spread reduces) on Monday back to Friday, excluding weekend data.

The idea is to be consistent.

The rest of the weeks trades will be as per post #1.

--- 帖子 #245 ---
As someone asked about 5 p.m. Et, yes after you determine the range and take the 10% of it. Add the 10% of the range to the previous day's low and that is our entry point for the day to go long. Subtract 10% of the previous day's range to the previous day's high that is our entry for the day to go short. Remember if the day ends near to the lows we would only look to go long and if it ends near to the high's then we would look to go short only. And yes we would place our orders immediately after doing all the calculations and then placing our orders.

Regards,

Bksujal

--- 帖子 #266 ---
I think Bksujal's system is functional, based on chart obserations over the last month.  However, I believe there's a more conservative approach to consider that can yield 25+ pips per day.

Here it is:

Instead of focusing on the prior day's high & low, consider the prior day's close.  Thereafter, add 20% of ATR (5) for a long position and subtract 20% of ATR (5) for a short position.  Include TS of about 35, with a TP of 45 and a SL of 40.

Test it... it works...

Thanks,

Walt

--- 帖子 #272 ---
Enter 5 units (5 minilitots, 5 lots, 5*0.2 minilots, whatever).

Long: Prev days (Close at 22 GMT) High + 1 pip Short: Low - 1 pip

Take profit as follows 1st unit at 15% of the daily ATR(14) + Entry, 2nd unit at 30% of the daily ATR(14) and so on. Leave unit 5 till the end of the day if in profit or leave to the next day if in loss and SL hasn't been hit.. Enter next units as described.. (You can have many unit 5s if you do not close them consecutively). Move to breakeven the SL of ALL units if take profit 2 has been hit.

I have found an error in my calculations but the result doesn't changes much.

Hope this helps.

bullrock

--- 帖子 #285 ---
You're right except that DST wouldn't account for it.

He has it marked off at 20:00 GMT.

Right now that is 1600 EDT (4PM). During EST that would be 1500 EST (3PM).

He must be under the impression that the time stamps on his chart indicate ET, when they actually don't.

EDIT- It just occurred to me what he's doing. He is showing 1H charts. The vertical lines are placed at the 20:00 GMT bar. The 20:00 GMT bar ends at 21:00. He computes his H and L between the vertical lines and places his trade at the opening of the next bar. That would be at 1700 EDT.

He is correct. His charts do not contradict what he has been saying.

--- 帖子 #298 ---
Bksujal indicated he was using ATR(14) on an hourly chart.

This means he is looking at the 14 bar average of the average true range of the hourly candles.

In other words- he's looking at the hourly candle range averaged over 14 bars.

How he uses that, I don't have a clue. He must use it to calculate his PT and SL, but I don't know how.

Here we go

For example.

Risk on each trade no more than 1-3% of your account.. Like say the ATR(14) is 100 say your SL is 50% of that so you risk capital*3%/50 per point. Then you say if 50% of the ATR(14) in gain then you trail your SL to break even and you close 1/3 of you rpositions when 100% of the ATR(14) is your gain the you close further 1/3 of you positions. and leave the rest till the end of the day....

One approach

--- 帖子 #327 ---
Hi CMartin,

I'm refining my numbers... stay tuned... There are two factors that we can rely on: (1) the prior day's close will be about the same as the new day's open; (2) Depending on the currency pair, it will range 90 - 160 pips during a 24 hour period. Instead of using the ATR (5), I'm taking the prior day's close, then adding 15 pips to determine the long entry position, while subtracting 15 pips to determine the short entry position. Because I do not know which direction it will trend during the next 24 hours, I enter both orders. Depending on the daily range pattern of the currency pair. My SL will range from 30 pips to 60 pips, while the corresponding TP will range from 40 pips to 70 pips. My intent is to hold the positions for up to multiple days if necessary.

Upon reviewin my results from yesterday, I noticed that if I had a LARGE SL (i.e. > 60), I would have obtained my TP on 7 of 8 trades, which each currency pair having 2 trades each (1 - long & 1 - short). The problem was that I got stopped out before the retracement occurred.

A classic example for a large SL occurred on 9/7/07 @ 1:29 GMT, when I entered a long position on 4 lots of EURJPY. Subsequent to that entry, my floating loss reach more than $4,000, as I had no SL. However, by today, 5 days later, they completely retraced to my TP of 25 pips. I think that it's best to have a SL, but in this case any SL less than 100 would have been to my detriment.

Currently, I'm focusing on GBPJPY, GBPUSD, USDJPY, USDCHF, EURJPY...

Walt

--- 帖子 #328 ---
I don't think bksujal's system quite says that tomorrows market will do the opposite of the close.

For a short, it says that if tomorrows market approaches today's high by a certain number of pips, it will retrace a certain number of pips.

How many pips it will retrace is anybody's guess. We can't get that out of him yet.

--- 帖子 #348 ---
The ATR is a very important indicator that show you the volatility of the market and give a real time coefficient in the chart. This numer (for example 0,0017) can be use to set a realistic and reliable SL, simply multiplying this number with your entry (if near the current value of the pair).

I have made some statistical analysis. Here are the HARD FACTS. Probabilities or odds if you wish. You remeber? I always stress.

Now here is the problem

Out of 2073 days analysed of the GU.

The probability that it will reach 15 pips from previous high is 831 to 199

The probability that it will reach 30 pips from previous high is 641 to 389
The probability that it will reach 50 pips from previous high is 439 to 591

See the problem??? It is 57% probable that it will !!NOT!! reach the 50 pips from top... Now we also have an extra 5 pips.

DOOMED to FAILURE if you do not push the SL to BE when the second TP has been hit. It is even better if there is a fourth unit to increase the odds... The mas rise from previous high during this analysed period was 359 pips in a single day. Are you going to leave that on table. Nope. 4th unit is the answer.

Regards

Bullrock or "Billrock"

--- 帖子 #382 ---
Based upon my visual observation of the daily candles over the last 3 months, only 1 out of every 5 - 8 trades results in a loss under the following conditions: (1) SL: 100; (2) TP: 30 - 50 (depending on currency pair); (3) No trailing stop; (4) allow for swing trading (1 or more days) before TP is reached; (5) enter long at prior day's high + 5 pips & enter short at prior day's low - 5 pips.

I've observed that about 60% - 67% of the daily candles have trended in accordance with the prior day close. In other words, if the prior day's candle closed higher than its opening, then the next day's candle will have a 60% - 67% probability for also closing higher than its opening, which was the closing price of the prior day.

Simply taking advantage of this pattern can easily yield four wining trades out of every five trades, or better.  Based on standard lot sizes, that's a profit of about $800 - $1,000 for every 5 trades - per day or per week.

I have been testing the following currency pairs: GBPJPY, USDJPY, EURJPY, USDCHF, & GBPUSD.

Please let me know if your backtesting or forward testing supports this assertion...

Thanks,

Walt

L+ -> if prev day close higher today close higher

L- -> if prev day close higher today close lower (pattern failure)

--- 帖子 #391 ---
Hi forexdummy.

Firstly, NO system can demand the market to conform to its parameters. In other words, we can never predict with 100% accuracy which way price will go.

The best we can do is devise a system based on probabilites provided by historical and forward tested data.

The D95P strategy is based on the probability of price continuing to our profit targets once it has moved beyond 5pips above or below the previous days high or low.

Some have mentioned that it has been historically shown that the market tends to 'range' (stay within the previous days high and low...or if it does breakout, retrace again within the previous days H and L) more than 'trend'(break above or below the previous days high and low and continue to trend). So according to this view, the probabilities are in favour of trading within the range of the previous day. You'll notice that discussion of BOTH approaches are contained in this thread.

Regarding your following statements:

The risk is the total amount of our stop losses.

'What if the movement really stroke down to the SELL point and continued going down?'

You seem to be describing the 'ranging' strategy that bksujal has shared...?

--- 帖子 #392 ---
Hi Bullrock,

I appreciate your technical analysis. Your data is very precise & detailed. However, you are not including a few variables that would change the percentage allocation for wins and losses. To use your terms (L+, L-, S+, S-), it's shortsighted to assume that all L- & S- equate to a loss. That is why a 100 pip SL is so important. With a SL-100 you can have a L- or a S-, but it can reverse to a L+ or a S+ within a few days as long as the SL was not reached. Another variable to consider is the fact that is some instances, although it may be a L- or a S-, the day's high or day's low was good enough to reach the TP before retracing to the L- or S-. Therefore, although it was a L- or S-, it was still a profitable day because it trended strong enough to reach the TP before reverting back to a L- or S-.

Once you factor in these other variables, I still believe that most of your trades in the trend will win 67% - 80% of the time with a TP-50 & SL-100.  I will try to provide emperical backtesting data to confirm my assertion.

Thanks,

Walt

--- 帖子 #421 ---
Hi, Walt, How can you yield 4 winning trades out of every 5 trades or better, given a pattern with 60%-67% probability? I think it should be 3 winning trades out of 5. Thanks!

[/quote] I've observed that about 60% - 67% of the daily candles have trended in accordance with the prior day close. In other words, if the prior day's candle closed higher than its opening, then the next day's candle will have a 60% - 67% probability for also closing higher than its opening, which was the closing price of the prior day.

Simply taking advantage of this pattern can easily yield four wining trades out of every five trades, or better. Based on standard lot sizes, that's a profit of about $800 - $1,000 for every 5 trades - per day or per week.

I have been testing the following currency pairs: GBPJPY, USDJPY, EURJPY, USDCHF, & GBPUSD.

Please let me know if your backtesting or forward testing supports this assertion...

Thanks,

Walt[/quote]

--- 帖子 #427 ---
Hello,

I've been following this thread with great interest from the beginning, and have even traded live with both systems, unfortunately to my loss. So, today, I spent a great deal of time trying to refine much of the information and ideas already presented here into a system that might work a little better, and with less complication.

It's a bit more conservative, and I've only tested it back for the last three weeks on GBP/USD to the beginning of September, but I'll present it anyway, in the hope that it might spark some greater intelligence, a few enhancements, and possibly increase our collective net worth. If anyone wants to back-test further, or wishes to comment constructively, please feel free to do so. Here are the rules:

SET UP:

1. One day ends while another begins at 2400 GMT. We trade each day at the closing price of the previous day, as recorded at 2400 GMT.  **See time reference after rules.

2. We trade Monday at Friday's closing price. Ignore all weekend price action and  ignore Monday morning gaps.

3. Determine the trend of the previous day, i.e., if the previous day closed higher than it opened, the trend was UP.

4. Determine range (by subtracting daily low from daily high) for previous day.

ENTRY:

1. Enter an order after the close of the 2300 GMT candle, at the closing price. This is the price at 2400 (midnight) GMT. A simple market order should work fine.

2. Enter with the trend. In other words, we buy long if the trend for the previous day was up, short if the trend was down. Only one trade for the evening.

3. Set TP=40, SL=40. For now, there are no secondary targets, as I want to keep things as simple as possible, to see if our entries work well enough to continue further discussion. For the record, in my tests many pips were left on the table after our initial target was hit.

FILTERS - DO NOT IGNORE:

1. If previous day's range was less than 100, DO NOT TRADE!

2. If the previous day's open and close were within 5 or 6 pips of each other, use the trend from the day before.

END OF RULES

----------------

Results for last three weeks:

9/3-9/7:      +160 pips

9/10-9/14:   + 80

9/17-9/21:   + 80

-----------

Total           +320 pips

**Time reference: 2400 GMT is the same as 8 PM (2000 hrs) EDT. When the U.S. returns to EST, this will become 7 PM (1900 hrs) EST. GMT does not change.

Disclaimer: I am only a novice trader, and could be way off here, so please exercise your own judgment before entering any trade based on this, or anyone else's system.

EDIT: I just tried this on EURJPY for the same period and it failed terribly.

Good luck to all!

--- 帖子 #433 ---
Thanks Jeff.

The rules are the same as in post #1. I've tried to remember to update it as new ideas or alterations have been introduced.

The only difference with my approach now is that of actively adjusting stops as profit targets are reached. I've added this as an option in post#1 for those able to monitor or manage their trades instead of using the set and forget approach.

So this opens up a whole lot of options...one may choose to raise stops to breakeven after the first PT is reached, or wait until the 2nd PT is reached before setting the 3rd order's stop at BE.... that's your call.

Though it means not being able to walk away and forget the trades for the day (unless you can trade from a pocket PC ), it will certainly prove more profitable and will definitely help to keep losses to a minimum. So I'm posting results accordingly to show what IS possible with this system.

rgs

mike

PS. I'm also demo trading the "ranging" strategy introduced by bksujal. It is a system in progress and the results are included with Daily95pips result updates.

--- 帖子 #435 ---
Hi vder.

Adjusting SL to BE is entirely up to your discretion.

Just to put the matter in perspective, I am only paper trading this system. Sometimes I won't even place a demo trade. I will simply calculate the entry levels and look back over the days price movement and see how the trades would have developed.

Based on this, it's easy for me to view the trades from a 'what if ' perspective. In a live scenario one would need to be much more diligent in monitoring the trades to be ready to adjust the SL to BE when the first or second PT have been reached. If alerts are helpful to do this then that's great.

This thread is merely to show what IS possible to achieve with this system.

The reality in a live situation will certainly be more challenging.

Yes, you are correct in that if SL are adjusted to breakeven the stop will then be only 15pips. Again, this approach opens up a lot more options. Remember that at this point we will have locked in +15pips of profit and will be eradicating any chance of a loss while leaving open a chance for another +80pips of profit. Alternatively, we could wait until the 2nd PT is reached before adjusting the SL to BE. Doing so would also leave open greater downside risk. So at the end of the day it's whatever you're comfortable with.

I hope this answers your question.

rgs

mike

--- 帖子 #448 ---
Hi Betees1.

Regarding timezones the following link may be helpful:

http://www.timeanddate.com/worldclock/converter.html

Essentially, you can place trades whenever you feel like it on whichever days, however following a consistent system / routine may be a better idea.

If 5pmEST is not a suitable time for you to be placing orders then the main thing to consider is having the orders placed before the European session starts. Orders placed before 2am EST should be 'safe' in this regard.

Regarding money management, please read the end of post#1. The total amount risked on any one trade should not exceed 3% of our trading account balance. So, regardless of the size of your account, trading in terms of % is better than thinking in $ terms. Money management is of equal importance to our trading strategy, though I have only touched upon it in this thread.

I have added you to yahoo msgr.

rgs

mike

--- 帖子 #467 ---
Hi andimozza.

If you'd like to experiment with your own version of the D95P strategy by all means do so. You may like to forward/backtest for results to ascertain if it is feasible.

It has been realised on this thread that to maximise results with D95P one would need to be more actively involved in monitoring trades and adjusting SL levels as profit targets are reached.

If you are wanting a simple set and forget strategy I recommend www.daily20pip.com

I've found (and the results show) that the higher profit target on the 3rd order of the D95P strategy, though not always achieved, more than compensates when it is.

I've also been careful to keep the risk:reward at approx. 1:1...in fact it's a bit better...there is the psychological advantage of knowing that even if one pair is stopped out at -90pips and another achieves +95pips I'll be up +5pips instead of breakeven. This gives the feeling of constant progress.

rgs

mike

--- 帖子 #482 ---
Hi mihat.

I suggest that you carefully read post#1.

We are placing PENDING orders at 5pips above AND below the previous days high and low (to be more precise, the previous 17hrs from 5pm EST ).

You are correct with your EURUSD example calculations, though remember that the pending orders have been placed before price reaches this level.

For example, today's orders for GBPUSD are Long: 2.0499 and Short: 2.0369. The previous high and low were therefore 2.0494 and 2.0374 respectively. So, pending orders have already been placed and we simply wait to see which of the long or short orders are triggered first.

We therefore DO NOT wait until price reaches these levels and then use MARKET orders.

I hope this answers your questions.

mike

Inserted Code
int h = TimeHour(TimeCurrent())+hourDiff;

if(h==3)
{
lowLast = CheckForLastLow()-5*Point;
highLast = CheckForLastHigh()+5*Point;
}

if((Ask == highLast) && orderToday == false)
{
OrderSend(Symbol(), OP_BUY, Lots, Ask,3,highLast-stopLoss*Point,Ask+tP1*Point,"",0,1200, Green);
OrderSend(Symbol(), OP_BUY, Lots, Ask,3,highLast-stopLoss*Point,Ask+tP2*Point,"",2,1200, Green);
OrderSend(Symbol(), OP_BUY, Lots, Ask,3,highLast-stopLoss*Point,Ask+tP3*Point,"",4,1200, Green);

if((Bid == lowLast) && orderTodayS == false)
{
OrderSend(Symbol(), OP_SELL, Lots, Bid,3,Ask+stopLoss,Ask-tP1,"",1,1200, Red);
OrderSend(Symbol(), OP_SELL, Lots, Bid,3,Ask+stopLoss,Ask-tP2,"",3,1200, Red);

orderTodayS = true;

if(orderToday == true && h == -2)
{
for(int i=0;i<OrdersTotal();i++)
{
if(OrderSelect(i,SELECT_BY_POS,MODE_TRADES)==false)break;
if(OrderType()==OP_BUY){
OrderClose(OrderTicket(),OrderLots(),Bid,3,White);
}else{
OrderClose(OrderTicket(),OrderLots(),Ask,3,White);
}
}
orderToday = false;
orderTodayS = false;
}

--- 帖子 #487 ---
You would need to use a BUY STOP and SELL STOP.  The above code, I believe, will enter the order immediately since you are entering prices above and below the current price, so it takes the current price.

A possible sample script is:

http://codebase.mql4.com/en/1024

EDIT:  Actually, after looking at this above script (TrendMeLeaveMe), this should already be setup to work for Daily95Pips.  You can draw a horizontal trendline on the high and low of the past 17 hours, set the Upper/Lower settings to your 5 pips, and it will automatically generate the buystop/sellstop orders for you (only when it enters into the zone).  The profit targets and whatnot may need to be added.

David

--- 帖子 #489 ---
Om.

I'm not sure how to add charts to a post...if you can advise me how that would be helpful.

Regarding deriving the high and low...it really depends on which broker you use and how the time is setup...

I use Oanda...so at 5pm EST I use one of two methods....either I'll open a daily chart, place the cursor on the last candle and take the high and low from the data box that pops up....or for Monday's orders I'll open a 1hr chart and look for the high and low going back to 00:00 midnight on the previous Friday morning.

The main consideration is that whatever you're approach for deriving the high and low (even if it is different to others) ,  be consistent.

mike

other way is to use the print screen button on you keyboard, push button, open PAINT (found under accessories in windows start), edit, paste, file , save as, j-peg or BMP, desktop.

once this is done

click the paperclip icon on the reply to thread/post and a new box opens, browes, desktop, selectfile, upload,

once uploaded, click paperclip and click on file.  Done.

hope this helps

MPP

PS if you right click on the file you save to desktop, you can open with picture editor if you have it and crop the image to the size you need (cut out the bites you don't want shown)  also in paint colour over the items like account numbers.

--- 帖子 #501 ---
Mike,

I had a problem using PrtScn in the past.  It turned out that it was due to my (wireless Microsoft) keyboard settings.  In order to access the PrtScn function, I had to press a key called FLock (may vary depending on brand of keyboard).  This turned FLock OFF, and then when I pressed Ctrl-PrtScn the current window was properly copied to the windows clipboard for pasting into other applications such as word and paint.  I thought I would offer this in case you were using a similar keyboard that locks the function keys by default to some other meaning like mine was.

Regards,

Greg

--- 帖子 #528 ---
Since we are still testing and there might be changes / improvements, I wanted to keep this simple. The more complicated the EA and the more variables it has, the more confusing things get. Once the system is set, it’s easy to automate it. So here’s what I’ve come up with, so far.

NOTE: Here it comes… EAs and Scripts here work on MetaTrader (MT4)… I don’t know about other platforms. Make sure you test it all on demo accounts first. I, anyone I know, anyone I have ever known, anyone I will ever know and anyone that I still don’t know and will get to know and those that they don’t know yet but may know or have ever known…is NOT responsible…blah, blah, blah… Anyway, obviously… Use these at your own risk.

If you want info on “Experts” (EA), how to attach, setup, etc…  and “Magic Number” info, please search the web. It’s all out there.

Step 1) Place “Stop Order Magic” into ~/yourBroker/MetaTrader 4/experts/scripts/  - folder

Step 2) Place “Trade Manager EA” into ~/yourBroker/experts/ - folder

Step 3) Open MT4 (close then re-open, if open now) and both files should appear in your “Navigation” window.

NOTE: To read instructions on “Trade Manager EA” settings, right-click it then “modify” – Opens MetaEditor and you’ll see instructions.

--- 帖子 #529 ---
1)Open 2 chart windows for the same pair.

2)On 1st chart drag “Stop_Order” script and enter inputs for “buystop”

3)Drag “Trade_Manager” to the chart and enter how you want this trade managed and be sure to enter the same Magic No. as assigned in step 2.

4)On 2nd chart drag “Stop_Order” script and enter inputs for “sellstop”

5)Drag “Trade_Manager” to the chart and enter how you want this trade managed and be sure to enter the same Magic No. as assigned in step 4.

NOTE: You can test many different scenarios on the same pair at the same time. Just open another chart window for the pair, use the script to enter the order and assign new Magic No and attach the EA to that chart, using the assigned Magic No.

There is your set-and-forget method. Set the orders and the EA and you’re done for the day. It will take your profits and move the stops along the way.

YOUR COMPUTER MUST BE ON AND TERMINAL OPEN FOR THE EA TO WORK.

-On “Tools > Options > Expert Advisors” tab…

-Make use “Enable Expert advisors” and “Allow Live Trading” is CHECKED and the 2 “Disable experts…” boxes are UN-CHECKED”

-Once attached, make sure you have the smiley face on top-right corner.

--- 帖子 #533 ---
For those sending PMs with questions regarding the EA and Script... I think it might be more beneficial if you asked them here, in the forum, as it may help those who might have the same questions but are afraid to ask .

No... You do not have to use the "Order_Script" if you aren't placing multiple orders on the same currency. You simply enter your order as usual, (market/stop/limit) then attach the EA and let it take profits and move stops for that trade... However, if you don't use the "Order_Script" and assign a Magic No. and later change your mind, your new order will be taken over by the EA, even if it's on a different chart of that pair. I hope that clears it up.

BTW... When you use the EA... it works off YOUR computer, NOT your broker's server. So your T/P and S/L levels are UNKNOWN to your broker... Just letting you know, in case you have a sneaky suspicion that the broker might be going stop hunting (which, of course, they never do ).

--- 帖子 #538 ---
Here is an excellent link for using MetaTrader: http://www.metatrader.info/node/27

Here is an excellent link on Expert Advisors: http://www.metatrader.info/node/34 (has lessons)

NOTE TO "EXPERTS" READING THIS. I have tried to make this post newbie-friendly and if you can add more newbie-friendliness, please do so

EXPERT ADVISORS 101: If you (1) turn off your computer or (2) lose web connection or (3) have EAs attached to charts in different “profiles” (MetaTrader still has bugs and limitations – it is a free platform),  Expert Advisors will NOT work. (Not only the one provided here but NONE of them).

This is why there is a script for manual order entry (and assigning Magic No) – so you are certain your order is set.. At the same time, it allows you the use the EA separately, to manage different systems simultaneously rather than have an EA that works for this system only.

In short, an Expert Advisor “Order” function only recognizes “buy” and “sell” and is set to place an order for THE PAIR, not for the particular TRADE for that pair. In METATRADER, you can place many orders for the same pair, but and EXPERT ADVISOR must be told WHICH trade on WHICH pair in order for it to recognize them as separate orders. Furthermore, METATRADER will allow you to attach the same EXPERT ADVISOR to the same chart only once. Otherwise, the EA would act EVERY TIME it ran into an order line (buy/sell) regardless of how you meant for it to be used.

This is why you assign a Magic No. It is basically a unique trade ID that you assign to a trade just like your broker assigns a ticket number to every trade. But the EA doesn’t recognize the ticket number, because ticket number is located in your broker’s server and the EA resides in your computer.

It tells the EA this: “I have 4 different scenarios going on in GBP/JPY pair. One is buying on break of high, the other is selling on break of low, and I want them all managed in a different way, to see which strategy works better. With assigned Magic No (script), I want you to use  an EA for this trade only and ignore all other buy/sell commands you run into along the way on this pair”.

EXAMPLE: Let’s say you want to test GBP/JPY  break of previous day high and low and you want to test 2 scenarios (using 1 lot as example) all on the same pair (GBP/JPY):

“script” = “Stop_Order_Magic” (provided earlier)

“EA” = “Trade_Manager_EA” (provided earlier)

You need:

(a)4 chart windows for GBP/JPY – any time frame.

(b)Window 1: Use script to place “buystop” – assigning Magic No 11111 - then attach EA to mange it – using Magic No. 11111 (i.e. close entire position at +30 with stop at -30)

(c)Window 2: Use script to place “sellstop” – assigning Magic No 22222 - then attach EA to mange it – using Magic No. 22222 (i.e. close entire position at +30 with stop at -30)

(d)Window 3: Use script to place “buystop” assigning Magic No 33333 - then attach EA to mange it – using Magic No. 33333  (i.e. close .2 lots at +20, close .2 lots at +40, close .2 lots at +60, close .2 lots at +80, close .2 lots at +100, with initial stop at -30, move stop to break-even at +30, move stop to +20 at +50, etc…)

(e)Window 4: Use script to place “sellstop” assigning Magic No 44444 - then attach EA to mange it – using Magic No. 44444 (i.e. same as in “d”)

(f)Then you may have a MA cross system you’re testing

(g)Then test a box breakout on 0:00 GMT

(h)Then test a box breakout on London Open

… and so on. All tested on SAME pair, but requiring its own window and a separate Magic No. (I have a little code system taped to monitor with Magic No utilizing date and a combo of numbers and then just keep recycling the same numbers the next day – OR – you can just add a LABEL to chart window to see which number you assigned).

You can manage as many different trades as you want on the SAME pair on as many pairs as you like. Without Magic No though, an EA will view EVERYTING in steps (b) – (h) above as ONE order and keep acting EVERY TIME it runs into one of those settings.

CAUTION: If you assign the wrong Magic No. or make a mistake when entering it into the EA, the smiley face on top right WILL still appear and FALSELY make you think your trade is beeing managed. Make sure you enter it correctly.

ONCE THE STRATEGY WE’RE TESTING HERE IS WELL TESTED and the “what-ifs” are reduced… then we can design an EA that will (a) calculate the entry (b) assign Magic No (c) Manage the trade (d) Cancel other open orders (e) Take profits and move stops all by just attaching it once at the start of the day. However.. that requires a lot of time and a LOT of testing and working out the bugs before it can be trusted on its own and I'd rather be trading than troubleshooting EAs. So, let’s fine-tune this strategy first, then work on making the mechanics of the trade easy.

Phiewwww…. I’m wiped, It’s a good thing it’s Columbus day and market is slow.

--- 帖子 #541 ---
A few days ago mike asked me to write EA for Daily95pips strategy.

I can see that pipimo88 has also prepared some other EA, but as I don't like having my projects unfinished, I present here the first version of my EA.

Is is totally automated system. Just add it to your H1 chart, enter parameters and let it work.

Do not use it on your live account now! It's the first release and quite a few bugs may come out.

To make it work you can either:Download mq4 file, copy it to 'experts' folder (located in your MetaTrader platform directory) and compile it. or Download ex4 file, copy it to 'experts' folder. Than restart MetaTrader if necessary and you can find the EA in Strategies node ready to use.

Parameters:FixedLots - amount of lots used for each order. If this is set to 0.0, Risk value will be used. Risk - per cent of capital used for each order. For 0.01 value each order will use the amount of lots equal to 1% of your free margin, i.e. for the total of 3 orders it will take 3% of your balance. Margin - number of pips added to /substracted from day high/low. By default it is set to 5. StopLoss - initial stop-loss value. TakeProfit1, TakeProfit2, TakeProfit3 - take profit values. DayStartHour - hour in your time zone that starts the forex day. LookBackHours - numbers of hours that EA looks back determining day high/low. OrderExpirationHours - number of hours after which buy/sell stop hours will expire. CloseOrdersNextDay - set to true, if you want to close open orders at the end of the day. EA with default settings works according to the rules stated int post #1.

Additionally:When buy orders are triggered, sell stop orders are deleted. And vice versa. (One-cancels-other function). Stop loss is moved to break-even point after reaching first take-profit. That would be it.

Waiting for your remarks.

Cheers,

Pr1mer

--- 帖子 #553 ---
The EA will manage a MAGIC NUMBER... not an "order". You place an order and assign a Magic No. to it for the specific purpose of having THAT order managed by THAT Magic No. If you just place an order straight from MetaTrader, the EA won't know what to manage.

Use the "order_script" to enter that order and assign a Magic No. just so it's assigned. Just put a label in the corner so you know what No. you assigned. You don't HAVE to use the EA. But if you need to walk away in a hurry, you can just set it later because Magic No is already assigned.

If you want to have a "hard" S/L and T/P set along with your order, then use the script to place the initial order and assign Magic No. Then in your terminal, open the placed order to "modify" it and set the hard S/L and T/P. If later you use the EA to manage it, your EA settings or hard T/P will trigger, whichever is hit first.

THIS IS ACTUALLY A GOOD PRACTICE, when using EAs, as a safety measure to have the S/L and T/P placed directly with broker. That way if you lose power in the middle of night and EA stops managing, you still have a safety net.[/quote]

If you use the EA and assign Magic No 11111, then finish that trade, right-click the "smiley" > properties > remove... to remove that EA and start a new one next time you place an order. The EA remains attached and remembers the OLD Magic No. until you REMOVE it (you must have used 11111 before and didn't remove the EA from the chart for the new order)... don't just change properties and enter a new Magic No. for the old EA. Attach a new EA to the new order.

This is why I provided an "order" script separate from the trade manager (EA). So people actually learn how this stuff works.

Hope that helps.

--- 帖子 #561 ---
HidaBull,

This system is simply based on the probability of when price breaks above or below the previous days high or low and continues in the direction of that trend.

There has been discussion to the effect that the market tends to 'range' within the previous days high and low more than it 'trends' by 'breaking out'.

So regardless of the parameters, just bear in mind that this is just another 'system' to follow with discipline, and if the results are good then we're all happy.

mike

Thanks Makepeace for sharing the spreadsheet.

The results are somewhat reassuring however inconclusive if the stoploss is not included into the calculations.

The reality is that price often does retrace just after triggering entry, even before the first profit target is reached. So we can therefore conclude that a certain % of the trades shown on the spreadsheet would have to accommodate this scenario.

Yesterday's trades are a good example....both EJ and UJ retraced and stopped out before the 1st PT was reached...

It's great to see that you've done this analysis, and if it's possible to factor in the 30pip stop that would be even better.

Hi BlindMist.

I am currently taking the results of the EA being used in a North Finance and ODL demo accounts.

The EA is programmed to move the stops to breakeven after the first profit target of +15pips has been reached.

I've considered the use of trailing stops however the broker that I started testing this strategy with (Oanda) does not provide them. --- 帖子 #636 ---
Using trailing stops on MT4 (InterbankFX) you need to be 1 pip past your profit target for it to work. ie: when you hit 16 pips it will trail to 1, 17 to 2, etc. It also needs to be on each order.

Thanks for all the work on this thread!

rion

--- 帖子 #642 ---
I just came across this thread and I was amazed to see that the system espoused is VERY similar to one I use.

I trade 4 pairs: GBP/USD, USD/CAD, EUR/AUD, GBP/JPY.  I chose these pairs because for the most part they are non-correlated.

I enter 2 trades on each pair:

- Long on daily high + 5 pips (10 pips for GBP/JPY)

- Short on daily high - 5 pips (10 pips for GBP/JPY)

I have a SL of the 33% of the 22-day ATR

and a TP of 66% of the 22-day ATR.

For GBP/USD that means that I have a SL of about 50 pips and a TP of about 100 pips.  And for GBP/JPY I have a SL of about 90 pips and a TP of about 180 pips.

When the market is trending I make out like a bandit, however when the market is ranging (like is was for the 1st 2 weeks of October) I get killed.

I'm currently working on trying to incorporate daily ADX to determine when the market is trending or ranging.  I'm thinking that I'll only enter trades when ADX is above 25 and sloping up.  I'll stay out if ADX is sloping down.  I haven't tried this yet, but I'll start next week.  Hopefully it will help me stay out of the market when I know my strategy doesn't work.

I'm also trying to come up with a way where I can take partial profits (like the OP does) along the way; but I want to keep my 2:1 win:loss ratio and I don't want to have my SL too close.  I like to give the market a little "breathing room".

Anyway, I couldn't help putting in my $0.02 because my strategy is so close to the OPs.

--- 帖子 #647 ---
Daystarthour - hour in your timezone/used by your broker when the forex day starts = when you want your stop orders placed.
Lookbackhours - how many hours to look back when calculating day high / low
OrderExpirationHours - after how many hours do stop orders expire.

Pr1mer

--- 帖子 #687 ---
Hi,

New version of EA is ready.

I have finally fixed problem with using EA for multiple pairs.

Additionally, I have added trailing stop feature and possibility to adjust break-even move.

Below I'll describe new settings, for others look for description in post #541 (http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=541).

UpdateToBE - number of pips in profit, when stoploss is moved to break-even point, e.g. when set to 15 - stop loss will be moved to opening price after reaching 15 pips profit. If you want to move SL to b/e when first take profit is taken, set to the same value as TakeProfit1 setting. The same goes for TP2, TP3.

UseTrailingStopOnLastOrder, TrailingStop - these are tricky ones

When UseTrailingStopOnLastOrder is set to false, there will simply be no trailing stop for last order  So take profit will be taken at the value of TakeProfit3. TrailingStop setting value is insignifficant in this case.

When UseTrailingStopOnLastOrder is set to true, trailing stop will be activated when order reached TakeProfit3 pips value. Trailing stop value is then equal to TrailingStop setting value.
Example:

We have TakeProfit3=50, UseTrailingStopOnLastOrder=true, TrailingStop=20.

Let's assume that buy orders were opened at the price of 1.2350. At the level of 1.2400 we'll have 50 pips of profit (for simplicity of this example spread is not taken into account). From now on, whenever price goes up, stop loss for last order will be moved to 20 pips below actual price. For example, let's take such sequence:

1) price - 1.2400, sl - 1.2380

2) price - 1.2405, sl - 1.2385

3) price - 1.2402, sl - 1.2385

4) price - 1.2407, sl - 1.2387

5) price - 1.2405, sl - 1.2387

etc.

EAMagicNumber - for advanced users only. It is a random number generated for this EA. Change is when using other EAs for the same account and they happen to use the same magic number (very unprobable). There's no need to change this value for different pairs - EA attached to a chart will only manage orders with magic number equal to EAMagicNumber setting and symbol correstponding to this chart.

I did some forward testing, but it's still not enough. That's where your role begins

Waiting for results, options, etc.

Have a nice weekend

Pr1mer

First I would like to say that this is a great thread. It has taken me a couple of days to digest all of the information and come to grips with the logic of this system. I would also like to say that Pr1mer is one of the best programmers I have ever met in one of these forums.

Having said that I would like to offer the following. I only use IBFX for my demo trading and have had a lot of experience with them.

If you are using IBFX you will need to set your DayStartHour to 21.The IBFX demo server is currently on EST+4 hours.

The second problem with IBFX is that they do not start their trading day on Sunday until 18:00 EST. Using the Expert for this system will not generate any trades for the Sunday/Monday session since it is set to put in the orders at 17:00EST. I have made a change to the expert to take this into account.

Also, when using IBFX, you will only look back 16 bars for the Sunday/Monday session buystop and sellstop orders since there is an hour missing with their 16:00 EST close on Friday and their 18:00 EST open on Sunday.

I have altered the expert to take this into account as well.

Please be advised that the expert that I have attached is the .04 current version of Pr1mer's expert with changes that only work with IBFX. It must be attached to your chart and active Sunday @ 18:00 EST - 18:59 EST to get the first days trades set.

I would like to close by saying that if Pr1mer does not want anyone altering his/her programming, please let me know and I will not post any changes again.  His/her programming knowledge is far superior to mine and I would not want to offend him/her in any way.

I hope that my input is helpful.

--- 帖子 #733 ---
Backtesting in MT4 for this system will not work for a few different reasons:

1) The time changes that go on during the year will change the calculations.

2) The only way to truely backtest a system in MT4 is to import tick data and use it on a 1M chart. In order to do this the EA would need to be rewritten to account for using a 1M chart. The tick modeling that is used by MT4 on the 1 hour charts that you get is from 1M data and the program basically guesses how the ticks went within the 1H bar and 1M bar based on the smaller time frames. The key to this is that MT4 GUESSES/MODELS the ticks. This is why the backtester is not trustworthy the way it is currently used by most people.

Hope this helps!

--- 帖子 #736 ---
Thanks for links giraia.

Hmmm...yes, the strategy is similar in that the setup is the same (5pips above and below the high and low) however the stops and profit targets are different, and multiple profit targets are not used by hans123. D95P moves stops to BE after the 1st PT has been reached, thus locking in partial profits...hans123 system moves stops to BE after price has moved somewhat (according to the pair) however it's still possible that the trades will stopout without ANY profits. Both strategies have the potential of stopping out for a loss....

Regarding:
If a certain position is taken and price turns                against you and it breaks the other side of the breakout channel                then turn. If the breakout channel is broader then the stoploss                first the stoploss will be hit. If the breakout channel is                narrower then the stoploss then hitting the other side means that                you have to turn your position. There is only one turn per time                frame possible. This rule is a result of all previous rules. You                can skip this rule if you want.

I'd definitely be inclined to skip this rule and would not be surprised if this was the cause of the large drawdown. I don't see the point in trying to 'chase' price. If price movement triggers the orders and reaches profit targets that's very good...if it doesn't I'm happy to move on and wait for the next day.

Another consideration that comes to mind is the pairs chosen. One of the objectives with the D95P thread is to shortlist the best performing pairs with the parameters of this strategy. Surprisingly, of the 2 pairs suggested for hans123 GBPUSD hasn't made the D95P shortlist....however EURUSD has.

At the end of the day I see the only mildly accurate similarity being the initial setup ( 5pips above and below the high and low).

That being said, any mechanical system is always subject to performing better of worse depending on market conditions and I thank you for bringing this to my attention.

rgs

mike

--- 帖子 #738 ---
I am going to state this again just so everyone gets the same clear picture:

YOU CANNOT BACK TEST THIS SYSTEM WITH THIS EXPERT!!!

If you run this expert in the backtester on a 1M chart it will only look back 17 minutes before it is suppose to place the orders! This is why it will not work. No matter what chart you run this expert on it will only look back 17 periods (or in other words, bars) prior to placing the pending orders for the day. If you run it on a 1H chart the tick modeling is not accurate, no matter what the modeling quality is. So please do yourself a favor and stop trying.

In regards to the period converter for MT4, it is designed to make larger period bars from smaller period ones. Example, 1H bars from 30M or 30M from 1M.

Over the weekend I will try to make some adjustments to the expert and make one for testing purposes only.

Hope This Helps!

--- 帖子 #749 ---
Giraia_br,

Yes I am using the expert exactly the way that I posted it with the exception of using fixed lots. You can change the FixedLots from 0.0 to .10, or what ever you want, to trade in the same lot size all of the time. You can leave the FixedLots = 0.0 and the expert will automatically risk 1% of your margin account for each trade. You can also change the Risk from .01 to a larger or smaller amount. Do not change the Margin because this is the setting used to decide how far to move the BS and SS above and below the high and low.

Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #760 ---
When you want to use EA for different pairs just drag the EA on the charts with these pairs. This creates different instances of EA for each pair.

Each EA manages orders that have corresponding EAMagicNumber and current chart's symbol, so you do NOT need to change this setting when using only this EA for different pairs (although you can, like PipHunter196 does).

This setting is handy when you want to use this EA several times for the same pair or with other EAs (just check if it's not using the same magic - highly unprobable).

Hope this helps.

Cheers,

Pr1mer

--- 帖子 #767 ---
The reason for this is that you have the trailing stop turned on for the third order. Thus it will not have a take profit since the stop will be your exit.

Turn it off and that should change.

You also do not have your time set up correctly. It should be entering at 17:00 EST which is 21:00 GMT. If your broker is on GMT you need to change this as well.

I am trying to work on the ODL USD/CHF Problem as well.

--- 帖子 #798 ---
Don't become a believer in back testing.  There are many instances of EAs that do good in back testing, but then do poorly in forward testing.   And vice versa.

Also, if you want to learn more about different EAs, and how to code new EAs, go to:

www.forex-tsd.com

Forex Factory also has a section that is good for EA matters as well, it's under Meta Trader 4.

http://www.fxprogrammers.com/

--- 帖子 #818 ---
Hello Everyone,

In this post, and the following, you will find the EAs that I have changed to work with the following brokers:

IBFX (InterbankFx)
Alpari
FXDD
North Finance
ODL

These need to be loaded on your platform and activated PRIOR to the start of trading Sunday, or whenever the first 1H bar for your broker is formed for the week. This EA is setup to work on a 1H chart. If you attach it to any other time frame, it will not trade according to the rules set forth by Mikelath.

Each EA has been modified to the time changes for each broker that I have listed above. They also take into account if the broker has missing bars from their close on Friday and their open on Sunday.

Pr1mer wrote this EA and deserves the credit for doing so. I am just trying to help with the time issues and, thus, I have made a couple small programming changes. His instructions on how to set up the other parameters are HERE.

If we can get everyone on the same time schedule, we can start checking other aspects of this EA. If there are any changes that need to be made after we start using the Fall Versions of the EA I will let you all know.

Have A PipFull Day!

--- 帖子 #834 ---
5pm EST (New York) as per post #1 is the time that orders are placed, taking the high and low of the previous 17hrs from 5pm EST ( New York ).

5pm EST( New York ) now equates to 8am in Brisbane, Australia.

If you are struggling with time conversion please click on the following link:
http://www.timeanddate.com/worldclock/converter.html
