--- 帖子 #861 ---
"UpdateToBE - number of pips in profit, when stoploss is moved to break-even point, e.g. when set to 15 - stop loss will be moved to opening price after reaching 15 pips profit. If you want to move SL to b/e when first take profit is taken, set to the same value as TakeProfit1 setting. The same goes for TP2, TP3." - Pr1mer

Maybe you should try to increase the UpdateToBE by another 10 or 20 pips.

--- 帖子 #868 ---
Though I welcome additional strategy thinking.  One of the more exciting features of this system is the greater than 1:1 Risk/Reward ratio each day on a set and forget methodology.  Total pips risked 90 best total gain 95.

The strategy you have posted has a less than 1:1 ratio.  Risking 75 and gaining 70.  This means you need a greater than 50% win rate just to break even.  Be careful there.

I was executed on EURJPY in both directions. Is it OK, or should I remove short orders after long execution?

Hi,

Execution in both direction will cancel each other out, except for broker fees (spread), which are two-fold...till one is stopped out first.

Dump the position & wait for another go-round.

--- 帖子 #895 ---
Hello rswamy4449,

The reason that some orders are canceled is because when the stops in one direction are triggered, the stops in the other direction are canceled. Example, if the BuyStop Pending Orders are triggered, The SellStop Pending orders will be canceled (or deleted).

Hope this helps!

Have a Pipfull Day!

--- 帖子 #907 ---
Hi fellow pipsters.

Some of you may be wondering why I got +407pips on Friday and you didn't....

After repeated experiences of having the 2nd and 3rd orders being stopped out after the EA moved the SL to BE once the 1st profit target was reached I decided to change the UpdatetoBE setting from 15 to 30, meaning that the EA now moves the stoploss to breakeven only after the 2nd profit target of 30pips is reached.

This has worked well so far, however be aware that it also exposes the trades to more potential loss ie. once the 15PT is reached and price retraces to the -30SL the result will be -45pips instead of locking +15pips if the SL had been moved to BE after the 1st PT was reached. The upside of course is that the 2nd and 3rd orders now have more room to move in achieving their profits which is what happened on Friday.

I'm also using the trailing stop feature on the 3rd order.

Tweaking of this system continues and I'm still over the moon about Pr1mer creating such a great EA !

rgs

mike

Hi Tim.

I'm not really inclined to do a backtest in order to determine which days of the week have performed better than others, as this average could just as easily change again as further forward testing is done. If you'd like to do this exercise then be my guest as all the daily and weekly results are on this thread to help you with the calculations. Have fun.:

So far I've found that good results can come on any day, therefore I leave the potential for profits open for the full 5 days, Mon-Fri.

Regarding the worst possible scenario for the day, well it happened today with EJ, UJ and EU all stopping out for a total loss of -270pips. I think this is the first day it's happened. The worst possible scenario on a longer timeframe would be if this repeated everyday until my trading account is blown.

So yes, this is also possible though not very likely. The best MM pertaining to this strategy is the use of multiple profit targets, moving the stoploss to BE after the 1st or 2nd PT is reached and using a TS on the 3rd order.

If you can think of anyway to improve upon this MM system I'm sure we'd all appreciate you sharing it.

Having said all that, I'll keep praying for success.

I used Fib s\r to adjust the EU third order tp. The attached image shows the tp as set by the ea to slightly below -61.8, a major support. There is every chance that a price will rebound from this, so I set my own tp a couple of pips higher. As things turned out, the price broke the barrier so I lost a couple of pips; another day I might have saved myself some profit.

I also checked that the stop losses were not affected. For example, a sl on a sell just below a resistance point could save the trade if moved beyond that point. The negative is that I could lose a few more pips if the price continued rising, but the image is a great example of s\r at work.

After the thick red candle, there is a faint, hard-to-see thin green candle where the price spent an hour bouncing between -23.6 and -50 before finally making up its mind and falling later on. You will need to enlarge the image to see the candle.

I offer these thoughts as a possible refinement for those able to monitor the positions once the ea has opened them. I have attached a great Fib indicator, courtesy of Spud, which shows the s\r points in detail. It is worth  changing the colours to white to make it more legible.

--- 帖子 #925 ---
I don't have an answer, yet - but it looks like the market filling in the gaps got me anyway.  I hope I am not boring you, but let me take a second to explain why this is a problem

When the market closes on Friday and then reopens on Sunday, it often opens at a price different than it closed.  This 'gap' can be anywhere from a few to a lot of pips.  If the market closed anywhere near the low or high from the previous day, the pending orders would be filled.  The problem is that the market tends to reverse and fill in these gaps, often times to just to reverse again and move back the original direction.   I even think there is a thread talking about how to trade these gaps

If your settings are as mine, the EA opened and filled orders based on the gaps, then hits the stop loss as the market reverses and fills in the gaps.

When I have some time, I am going to go back and see how often this has been occuring.  The only answer I can think of right now is to turn off the EA and skip using it on the first day of the week.

Any other thoughts?

Tim

Hi Kevin.

If you are manually trading this strategy you may find using the calculator at post#863 helpful.

At 5pm EST simply look back at the previous 17hrs and take the highest point that price has reached and the lowest as well. Input these figures into the calculator which will do all the calculations for you and then simply place the orders with your broker.

I hope this simplifies the process for you.

--- 帖子 #948 ---
Exactly. You look for high and low from the midnight to 5pm CET. (5:00pm - 17 = 0:00)

Then :

BUY pending order: HIGH + 5 pips + spread

SELL pending  order: LOW - 5pips

You have to add spread to your high calculation if you use ask price. If you dont apply the spread to the calculation your buy order will be lower (depends on spread) and executed sooner. If you use the calculator, apply "BID" price or "ASK + spread" price for correct calculation of your buy order.

--- 帖子 #960 ---
I should have left those eu trades open on my live account. They triggered on the demo and have made +45 now, with the third order still in place. The ea hasn't closed it; it should be placing my new trades in about 40 minutes, at 8.00 am London time.

I have been thinking about the losing trades - not that I have any yet.

From what I have learned, accepted wisdom is: 1) trading against the long-term trend is financial suicide; 2) the long-term trend is found by looking two time frames further on in the charts.

I have looked at the daily charts for eu (screaming upwards), uj (up but with a strong retrace) and uj (gone to hell in a handbasket). Mike, or any of the others who have been trading this system for a while, have you any idea how many of your losing trades were taken out in the opposite direction to the prevailing trend?

Fibonacci support and resistance could well be playing a part. For those of you unfamiliar with Fib s&r, it works like this. Suppose a pair is trending upwards like the eu. Eventually, it hits a Fib resistance point that traders regard as an important barrier to further progress, so they close their orders and take their profits. This causes the price to fall until it hits a certain point that traders (often the very ones who closed in the first place) consider will signal a return to the upward momentum; they will then go long again. Fib s&r points thus become self-fulfilling prophesies.

We can play with these points. There is a Fib retracement tool on the MT4 platform; look for the icon with 4 rows of dots and an F in the bottom right corner. Go to, say, the eu chart on any timeframe and look anywhere for a place where the upward movement of the last few weeks is interrupted by a downward movement. Click on the Fib icon, then on the chart at the bottom of the upward movement and drag to the top of it. You will see the Fib retrace points plotted on the chart. If you haven't done this before, you will be interested in the way certain points trigger counter-movement time and time again.

I like trading the 30 min chart for 20-30 pips; Fib 61.8 seems most important here. I love scalping for +5 on the 5 min chart, where Fib 100 is most important; once the price breaks this then making +5 is easy.

I don't know what the crucial point is on our 1H tf, but it will be one of the smaller ones; 38.2 or 23.6 are my guesses, as we are dealing with a longer time frame.

All this could affect this tradingsystem thus: a strong price retrace triggers the pending order; the retrace is at its apex, and so the price reverses back in the direction of the trend. Hey-presto, -90.

All my winning trades have been taken in the direction of the prevailing daily trend apart from the uj yesterday. Do a retrace thing on the daily, dragging from top to bottom of the previous downward movement, and you will see a retrace almost to the 38.2. I might simply have been lucky yesterday.

All of which is a long-winded way of suggesting that we cancel (ea) or do not set manually, the pending orders that are in the opposite direction to the trend as seen on the Daily chart. What do you guys think?

Steve

I for one am very pragmatic - if it ain't broke - don't fix it.

In stating the obvious, it is the trend reversals that cost pips using this system.  If having the EA initiate the pending orders at the opening of London means fewer revesals during the day, then the losses should also be fewer.

Does the EA still close all orders at the end of the trading day before the Far East markets open?  If so, one of the downsides I see is that the orders would have less time to do their thing.  It will be interesting to see what effect different 'start' times will have on the results.  Even more curious, will each pair have a 'best' time for the EA to initiate the pending the orders?  For example, maybe EURUSD works best when the orders are started at the open of London where USDJPY may work best when the orders are started at the open of New York.

The potential is endless - but the possibilities may my head hurt...

Any more thoughts....

--- 帖子 #987 ---
This could come down to us watching the trends and working out when the trend is retracing or about to retrace. For example, take a rising trend. The price could trigger one of our orders just before a retrace kicks in and wipes out the trade. Logically, we should be able to look at the chart and note when the rising price should be about to falter because the price rises in waves, yet we all know how difficult this is to do.

Ye Gods, anybody got any headache pills?

This thread started with a fire-and-forget strategy. Here we are trying to turn it into a fire-and-make-even-better strategy. Life isn't easy, is it?

Ok, my demo account has sent the pending orders at 22.00 gmt (5.00 pm est). My live account is set to do the same 10 hours later, at 8.00 am gmt (3.00 am est). It will be interesting to see what happens to the two sets of orders. Guess which I hope is right?

My best guess? Just as a trend is a trend or a blip depending on the time frame involved, so a breakout happens from whatever starting point is chosen or it doesn't. A breakout just prior to setting the pending orders automatically creates a fresh channel to set the orders by.

So, if the breakout is in the direction of the prevailing trend, then it is more likely to be a genuine breakout. If not, it is more likely to be a brief retrace. I am thinking about aloud here, and it is proving most useful. This encourages me to check the direction of the trend when looking at the orders the ea has set.

Hmmmmmmm. Simple, this forex business isn't it? The price goes up, so we buy and make a fortune. It falls, so we sell and make a fortune. If only.........

--- 帖子 #1003 ---
Thanks for the quick support and I will keep everyone posted as frequently as I can.  I will post results at least once a week.  I should also mention that doing anything special around news events would be a major amount of work such as disabling certain pairs when news is released which may affect certain pairs.  I will make my best efforts to track major news events and note them in the results I post.  If trades opened 3 hours ago and news hits there isn't much you can do about it anyways.

I think once time frames and pairs are selected then managing upcoming news events will be easier.  You could choose not to run the EA on certain pairs if news is close to coming out.

Also, I noticed that the S/L is set without considering the spread.  If a spread is 5 and you start -5 when the trade opens then you really only have 25 pips breathing room right from the start.  Is that the best way or should the spread be considered when setting a S/L?  Some ideas off the top of my head for EA mods might be...

Consider the spread.  Maybe a setting for max spread allowed?  In other words, you could say you don't want to trade unless the spread is less than or equal to say 5 or some other number.  IBFX can fluctuate a good deal throughout the day and even the EUR/USD can get a pretty wide spread at times.  I think this can have a tendency to hurt EAs because it can get out of hand at times and this would give us more control over choosing our conditions to trade.

Another setting (True/False) for spread to be included in the S/L calculation.  That way you can choose to use it or not.

I am a programmer so I added a line to show a chart comment showing me the start time and look back hours on the chart.  This and maybe some other items shown as chart comments are helpful in saving time so you don't have to check the settings manually.  It helps me when running 11 demo accounts each with 19 pairs running.  Future updates would be great with this added.

I haven't given the code a great deal of time when looking at it and would like to say that I think it runs well and does what it should.  Please don't take my wish list as a dig in any way.  I have programmed dozen of EAs myself and know what is involved.  My thanks to the programmer responsible for coding it.

I'll wait for Mike to correct me if I'm wrong, but I believe this is a mechanical system and as such once the orders are running you can leave them run regardless of news etc, that's what I've been doing. My feeling is that you could leave all the orders run through news without change - this would mean that all results you obtained should be robust, easily reproduceable and can be used as a worst case baseline.

Many people may feel my views are wrong and please let me know if you have better ideas?

--- 帖子 #1013 ---
I have a question in reguards to this trading idea.  I have been looking at this for several days now and love the idea of how this works.  As yoy have explained pending orders are placed at HIGH +5 and LOW -5,  That means if the market goes up and hits HIGH +5 then we now have three long orders on the pair.  If the market turns down then we have three pos at risk with a 30 pip stop loss on each.  Here is my idea and I am wondering if anyone has thought of this or tested this. Here it goes..... what if the three orders were placed at HIGH +5, HIGH +7 HIGH +9.  Then if the market hits the first one and it is triggered then goes down, the risk is only on one pos and NOT all three.  If in fact the market is going to go high enought to make a profit of all three for a total of 95 pips, then we would be giving up a couple pips profit. The way I see it is this might be a saft guard that would save a few losses.  What do you think and is it possible to back test this idea against the reg 95 pip plan.  I would be currious to see if running a back test against this if it would return more pips threw not losing pos.

I am looking forward to hearing what you guys think about this idea. I am going to begin to test this on my demo account as soon as the market opens.

What's the proper action in such a case? Open orders or shift stop orders?

Hi Corey.

The rules are as per post#1.

So far, I'm personally in favour of moving the stops to BE after the 1st profit target has been reached. This may or may not be the more profitable approach.  I haven't had a lot of extra pips from using the trailing stop, though theoretically it does keep open such potential.

My preferred settings for the EA are therefore UpdateToBE:15 and no trailing stop on the 3rd order.

Any open trades are let run for the full 24hrs.

--- 帖子 #1045 ---
Hi samoora.

Firstly, my avatar phrase "trading for living" is more of an affirmation of what I'm aspiring for (if that's the reason you're asking).

I am definitely progressing to the stage of live trading and generating enough income from that to at least get me started with paying the bills.

How much do you need in your trading account to generate your desired income ? Well, firstly that really depends on how much your lifestyle depends upon or how much you would like to earn or how much is really enough...

Secondly, you have to consider the system you are trading, and equally important, your money management in order to achieve your desired income whilst preserving your trading capital.

For example, if you are trading a system where the risk:reward is 1:1 you will need to assess how much of your account you are willing to risk on each trade. From what I can gather the standard amongst professional traders is that they will not risk any more than 3% on each trade. So if you had a $10,000 account the max. you would risk on each trade is $300. This would be the amount you would lose if the trade was a loser and also be your profit if the trade is a winner. If you were fortunate enough to achieve an average of 1 winning trade per day you would end up with $1500 over 5 days of trading. Sounds simple doesn't it....but whoa, don't get too excited yet, because the reality can be and often is very different. Just consider if your 1st trade is a loser and your account balance is now $9700. 3% of that is $291. So even if you win the next trade you are still $9 behind. This may seem insignificant but can contribute to your account being eaten away and requiring significantly more winners to recover when you have a string of losing trades.

So basically the 2 important elements are:

1. A winning strategy

2. Good money management.

This is a simplistic explanation of how to approach live trading. I cannot emphasise enough the importance of being aware of the downside risk and managing that risk in order to stay in the game.

Regarding the hans system, I do not trade it. There is very little similarity between it and the Daily95pips system.

I hope this helps.

rgs

mike

--- 帖子 #1087 ---
I am trading D95P live, & not with tiny pips either, it is working very well, thank you, Mike Lath.

I only trade EUR/USD , USD/JPY & the EUR/JPY, they have proven themselves & quite frankly any more pairs are just too hard to handle.

I trade manually & I place my trades at about 2100 GMT with buy & sell stops. I look back at how my trades progress around the Frankfurt/London open & adjust stops accordingly.

As the forex market is a 24 hour Market, I don't religously use the previous Days H/L for my calculations, If there was a swing H/L the previous 48 hours, I will Indeed use that, & especially if on the new GMT Day, it is just a continuation of the previous day, I go back to the swing point & use that as my reference & place that in my spreadsheet I gave you all earlier.

Also, if there is a large spread between the High & the low & the market is near a previous H/L & is close to taking me in, I won't place a trade in the opposite direction if it has to rally 200 or more points to take me in, hence, I trade the breakout in the direction of the trend, & allocate more money as per money management into this trade.

Also, look at earlier support/resistance, & significant levels, eg, EUR/USD at 1.5000, these whole numbers are VERY important.

As well I use Fibonnacci levels to aid my trading.

You just can't blindly trade a "system" you must use your skills as well, after all, the price is always right,

Bazza

Hello. It seems there are quite a few trading this successfully. However analyzing the formula, trading on paper, and with various backtesting, there are a few things that don't quite boost my confidence in trading this strategy. Many have mentioned that ranging markets would work best. Could someone please explain this, as I'm just not getting it. In a ranging market it is very likely to get losses on both sides. Would this not work better when price trends and is moving unidirectional? Even when price does move in one direction, it seems the likelihood of taking on losses is still very high. I think this system needs an improved method of taking back one's losses.

--- 帖子 #1111 ---
Hi GridTrader.

To a degree this strategy reduces our risk against the effect of a ranging market by having a relatively small first profit target whereby if achieved the stoploss on the 2 remaining orders is adjusted to breakeven. We do see that price will sometimes trigger the orders and then immediately retrace and stopout all 3 orders for a -90pips result.

Bear in mind that the EA has a OCO feature that cancels the long orders when the short orders are triggered and visa versa, eliminating the possibility of getting losses on both sides.

Earlier in the thread there was considerable discussion on the idea of the markets ranging more than trending, thus suggesting the odds being against the success of this strategy. I for one am always open to any positive alternative and a ranging system based on using ATR was touched upon, however not developed sufficiently for greater acceptance. For a while I simultaneously traded a basic ranging strategy along with the D95P system to compare results. There was an idea that one could hedge against the other. My realisation was that not only did the ranging strategy require a lot more development, both strategies tended to cancel out the results of the other. Thus it made more sense to rely on one or the other. Because my focus has been testing the D95P system which relies on a breakout from the previous days high or low I've maintained that focus in order to present clear conclusive results which form the real assessment of it's worth.

So despite the apparent odds being against this strategy based on it being a trending system rather than a ranging one, ultimately if it's providing good results then all other considerations are rendered less significant.

You're suggestions for improving this system are most welcome.

rgs

mike

--- 帖子 #1122 ---
A while back I was baffled as to why all and any trades I made, were set to break even after a few pips in my favor. It happened often enough that I finaly figured out that once any trades I entered made 15 pips, the SL was automatically set up to break even. It probably saved me some money, lol, but it also stopped me out of trades that would've been good trades. --- 帖子 #1162 ---
Hi mtaboneweb,

Thanks for setting up a reverse EA.  It will be interesting to test out.  I notice that you have set it out with orders based at the original third TP point (i.e. 50 pips out).

However if you consider your results the majority of failures occur when the entry orders are triggered and then the spot rate fails to go the 15 pips to the first profit level.  So I was wondering if you wouldn't mind setting the reverse system with the sell entry orders at period high +5 (as per Mikes rules) not +50, and the stop at period high +20 ...and the opposite for the buy entry orders below the low for the period chosen.

I was keen for a stop at high +20 since most of the failures come from price action not moving the additional 15 pips to the first profit level (above the high+5 breach point).  In this way we can minimise the loss and maximise the gain - since we will have the three profit levels still in place (for the breach of the high +5 pips, these would then be at high-10 pips, high-25 pips, and high-45 pips).

So we are then getting really good risk reward ratios here also.  And we could still have the stop to BE when the first pull back level (high -10pips) is reached.

Spreads will have to accomodated also.

Tim

--- 帖子 #1163 ---
Hi Mike,

A suggestion for a price filter would be to only allow the EA to set trades for pairs that are less than 1.2x of the previous days ATR(10).  With this we would be ensuring that trades were not be set for days that followed very big moves since they are often prone to pullbacks the following day.

Several years ago I worked on a breakout system that took an entry at the open of the new day plus 70% of the previous days ATR(10), and ran a stop of the open-50% of the previous days ATR(10).  TP was a time exit which we found best suited to 3 days out from trade entry.  (I am not the original system designer).

Results were good, but it would run several months in a row in DD sometimes (so it was best suited to the long term trader).  However we found that we could significantly improve the winning trades by including a price filter as I suggest above.

The logic being that breaches on days following a large candle day were much more susceptible to volatile whips as it made the breach of the previous days large range candle.

Maybe this could be considered for future versions of the EA as a possible filter to test??  (Possibly add as a variable to the inputs)

Tim

Spreads are considered when placing orders and the other settings can all be tweaked to whatever you like.

--- 帖子 #1190 ---
The IBFX version is the same except for an updated comment that is added to the orders.  The comment shown in the attached picture is a mod that I made to the original EA.  The example means:

11/30 - 0(950017)

Date the order was placed.
Start hour
This is the magic number (95 for Daily 95, 00 for start hour, 17 for look back hours)

I did this to help me sort things out once I save the detailed reports but you have to display the comments in the history tab to see them in the detailed report.  If an order is placed on 11/29 then it may not be triggered until 11/30 and the time would also change to when the order actually triggered.  It's just my way of preserving the initial information of the order.  I also change the magic number for each account (not currency) based on the start hour and look back hours.  My magic numbers are 950017, 951317, and 952217 to match my settings on each demo account.

The reverse comment would come out looking like this: 11/30 - 0 R (950017)

This will help me distinguish the trades further if I ever run a reverse and regular EA on the same account.

The EAs are compiled with their original magic numbers so you will need to change them manually if you would like it to be different.  It's one of the settings in the EA properties window.  For my demos I loaded my first chart and set everything the way I wanted it (i.e. magic number, fixed lot size, start and look back hours).  I then saved it as a template and applied that template to each chart I opened from that point forward for that account.  Just a time saving tip.

The magic number needs to be unique for each currency in a single account.  That means if you have 2 EUR/USD charts and the same EA attached then each should have a unique magic number like 952217 and 951317 if I were running both time frames on the EUR/USD with 2 charts on the same account.  I can have the same magic number if the currencies are different like if I was using the EUR/USD and some other pair(s) on the same account.

When the EA checks to see what it should do it loops through all the orders on your account and looks for those that match the symbol (i.e. EUR/USD) and the magic number.  I am over explaining for the benefit of anyone who has questions about what the magic number is used for and why it's important to an EA.  If anyone has questions or feels that I have confused the issue by over explaining please let me know.

Anyways, long story short, I forgot to add the "R" in the comment when I compiled it for the original post.  If you have to have the "R" then you will want the version from the most recent post.

--- 帖子 #1203 ---
Hiya Bob.

My understanding is that your computer must be turned on for the duration within the week that you would like the EA to function for. From what I can gather, the EA is attached to and functions from your computer, not the broker.You would therefore need to have the hibernate option switched turned off in the screensaver section of the control panel. The reason for this is twofold:

1. To ensure that the computer is on when the EA is due to calculate the new orders for the day.

2. To ensure that the computer is on to manage any open trades ie. executing profit targets and stops.

As for whether you need the trading platform to be constantly open for the EA to still work, I'm not 100% sure. Personally, I keep the trading platform open for the whole week (Sunday night to Saturday morning Brisbane time)and minimise it while I do other stuff on the computer.

If you are running the NF fall version the default settings are set to the 'standard' rules of the D95P strategy as per post#1. If you are happy with these settings then you don't need to change a thing. Pr1mer has programmed the EA to calculate order sizes based on a % of the account balance, thus achieving the desired money management objective. He has included a word doc with instructions outlining each setting ( sorry, I can't remember which post it's at ). The only difference between Pr1mer's latest version of the EA and PipHunter's fall EA's is that piphunter has adjusted the DayStartHour to suit numerous brokers who start the day at different times, thus making it easier for newbies unfamiliar with how to adjust the input settings on the EA. I'm immensely grateful to both of them.

rgs

mike

--- 帖子 #1206 ---
The platform needs to be running as long as there are open orders or pending orders.  The EA has to be active to manage the trades as the charts tick.  It's what is responsible for moving the stop loss to break even after +15 is achieved, trailing stops if chosen, etc.  It also closes the opposite trades.  The system would not produce good results without this maintenance of the orders.

--- 帖子 #1212 ---
Hi everybody - as always - thanks for the input and the hard work - you know who you are...

I am wondering if anybody has tried starting their orders, whether live or not, at the open of Tokyo market? If so, what have been the results?  In my IBFX live account (using teeny, tiny lots)  there seems to be a lot of price volatility when the volumes are thin.  This would seem to lead to more - saying this nicely - market manipulation.

I don't know if the thin volumes are working for us or against us.

2nd item - With the reversing - here is another thought.  Again, on days where we have had a big move in the market and the close is near the top or the bottom of that big move, the market always have a tendency to do some retracing.  We have the problem of orders getting triggered and then stopped out with this retracing. I believe this is being addressed with the reverse changes made in the EA.

The second piece of this puzzle is the fact that the opposite order is set way on the other side of this big move.  For example, let's say a pair moves 200 pips up in a given day.  Before our sell orders are triggered, the market would have to retrace the entire 200 pips plus 5 more (or whatever number you are using)  before our sells would be triggered.  Way into this 200+ pip move, the tide has obviously turned.

I have seen in several different places, the use of a calculation to determine when the market momentum has reverse.   The term used I have seen most is 'pivot point'.  The calculation of the pivot point is easy enough:

(Previous Period Close + Previous Period High + Previous Period Low) / 3

Most of you are far more experienced and smarter than I am, do you think a pivot point +or- 5 pips on the day after a big move might yield more pips?

Comments and input please....

Tim

--- 帖子 #1236 ---
Some of the issues I've had with this EA are below:

1. If the pending orders have been placed and you close and re-open MetaTrader while it's still within the hour to place the pending orders, then it places another set of pending orders.  The EA doesn't do a good job of checking to see if pending orders have already been placed.  The EA needs to check things out before it opens pending orders.

2. If you have double pending orders for a currency and one direction is triggered only 3 of the opposite trades are canceled leaving 3 others that could be triggered later in the opposite direction.  Double orders shouldn't happen in the first place but the EA should still be able to handle this situation.

3. If it turns out that moving the SL to BE is a lag issue where the broker somehow turns the order to modify down then the EA should re-try on the next tick of the chart until it can be set.

I also think that there should be an option in the EA to say true/false for directly opening orders if the currency is too close to the high/low to place pending orders.  In this case it would place direct trades in that direction and not even bother setting pending orders in the opposite direction.  Suggestions have been made to place x amount of pips even higher or lower but I feel if you're going to set it that close in the first place then you might as well get in sooner and have a better chance at your TP.  If you set it 5 above or below then you will most likely hit that anyways and you've already lost an additional 5 pips already in that direction.

Another idea... Has anyone considered setting the +50 TP's stop loss to +15 once the +30 TP order has hit.  In this case if you hit +15 and +30 and your +50 never happens then you would still have +15 for a total of +60 if it only went as far as the +30 marker instead of falling all the way back to 0 leaving you with +45 instead.  I realize that moving a SL up would possibly decrease the possibility that the +50 might have enough room to hit +50 but it does ensure more of a profit if it never makes it all the way.  I would rather take +15 more on the last order rather than wait for +50 which may not happen.  This may leave to small of a window for the maximum profit.  It could be added as a true/false setting in the EA.

Thoughts?

--- 帖子 #1237 ---
The magic number is not the issue as long as they are different pairs.  The EA looks for a match of the magic number and the symbol for the chart it's running on.

Under the options menu there is an Expert Advisor tab.  The 2nd and 3rd checkboxes from the top are what I'm talking about.  Allow live trading does not need to be checked here as long as it is checked on the EA's settings on the chart.

--- 帖子 #1262 ---
Hi leo9 and welcome to the D95P thread.

Yes, the strategy uses the high and low of the previous 17hrs from 5pm EST (which is 17:00 by 24hr time). So we are using the high and low of practically the whole day(17hrs), not for that hour only. Monday is the exception as weekend activity is often minimal, therefore we use the data going back to midnight Friday morning.

I suggest that you simply use the Expert Advisor to automate the trading of this strategy. If EA's are new to you then just ask for assistance and we'll guide you from there.

rgs

mike

--- 帖子 #1277 ---
I think it's good for people to experiment with different ideas on this strategy.  That's exactly what I'm doing.  At this point I am just keeping it simple and close to the original idea that started this thread.  I would also like to say that I believe back testing has proven to be flawed more often than it has been correct. I would not discourage anyone from running a back test and sharing but I would also ask that people don't jump ship just because someone got bad results in a back test. I am of the thinking that the only good way to test is with forward live testing.  Even under a great model quality in back testing is never more than 90% and live testing almost always proves to differ from back testing.

--- 帖子 #1291 ---
Here is my setup with the fall EA for IBFX and NF...

08-17 (London open)IBFX demo, 18 pairs, start hour set to 8 (Column B)

NF demo, 18 pairs, start hour set to 10 (8 GMT Column D)
13-17 (New York open)IBFX demo, 18 pairs, start hour set to 13 (Column F)

NF demo, 18 pairs, start hour set to 15 (13 GMT Column H)
22-17 (Original strategy)IBFX demo, 18 pairs, start hour set to 22 (Column J)

NF demo, 18 pairs, start hour set to 0 (22 GMT Column L)
The NF time is 2 hours greater than IBFX which is GMT time.  That's why the NF demos get set 2 hours greater.

Six demos testing 3 different start hours to compare which pair does good under which start time and then which broker did better than the other.

My results so far have been mixed showing certain pairs performing better with certain brokers.  Notice how the AUD/JPY produced 330 pips (9 days with an average of 37 pips) on the IBFX demo.  This pair did better than the North Finance demo under the same settings.  This could be due to lag, data stream, etc.

I have highlighted a few areas to point out some major differences that caught my eye.  Se the magenta highlighted area?  IBFX had 7 days it was triggered where the NF only triggered on 4 days.  This was due to the NF demo being too close to even set the pending orders so they were never made.  It show some differences between brokers because the IBFX demo had less problems setting the pending orders and then triggering them.

I use these results to pick out settings for certain pairs and possibly even certain brokers.

Are these results a benefit to anyone or should I keep it to myself?  I don't seem to get a lot of feedback from anyone looking at them except with questions about what they show.  I don't want to waste anyones time or create excessive posts when no one may be interested.

--- 帖子 #1309 ---
If you are running an IBFX demo or real account then the time in the software is GMT time in which case you would set start time to 8 if you wanted 8 GMT.  Your own time zone should not affect the time shown in the MetaTrader software.  If you are going manual then you'll have to do some work to figure the difference between your time and GMT.  Since I run IBFX and North Finance demos they are different.  IBFX is GMT so I would set it at 8 in the EA settings.  NF is 2 hours ahead so I set that for 10 in the EA settings.  The point is you want it to be based on GMT 0 not + or - anything.

--- 帖子 #1310 ---
It needs to be running period.  It wont place pending orders or do maintenance to existing orders if it's not running with the EA attached to the chart and the EA enabled.  An EA cannot work unless the software is running.  I'm only stressing this because people seem to ask this question a lot.  Each time the chart is updated (tick) it fires the EA which applies the logic within itself and does any needed actions.  If it's not running then it can't do anything and you most certainly don't want to turn off the software after pending orders are placed.  The orders will become active when the price is reached but without the EA running it wont cancel the opposite orders, adjust stop losses once  pips is hit on the first order, trail stops if selected, etc.

--- 帖子 #1311 ---
Correct..I should have clarified.  Thanks mtaboneweb!

--- 帖子 #1326 ---
Hi,

As a novice can i ask what may seem foolish to yourselves but not to me at this stage. This system is based on a set & forget basis eg set at time of trade , then leave and come back later hopefully with a bag of pips. So after setting the trades can i then turn off my PC + EA ? If so on  returning and switching back on the PC + EA will all calculations (profit totals) be inserted correctly ?

Thanks

--- 帖子 #1327 ---
You have to leave it running.  It is set and forget because the EA does all the work for you.  The EA is not only responsible for setting the pending orders but many other things as well...

Once a set of pending orders are triggered the EA closes the opposite orders.  If the buys are triggered then it closes the pending sells or vice versa.

Once the first 15 pips is achieved and that order closes at it's take profit then the EA moves the other 2 orders to break even on their stop loss.

If you have trailing stop enabled then the EA manages resetting the stop loss as the last trade moves.

All of these things would have to be done manually if it weren't for the MetaTrader platform and the custom EA that has been written to manage all of this for us.  Each time a chart is updated (tick) then the EA runs it's logic and does what is supposed to happen if anything at all at that point.  If the software isn't running and the chart isn't open and the EA isn't attached then the system cant to anything with the orders it placed.  Dozens of people ask this same question on nearly every thread here.  If you set your alarm clock and then unplug it will it go off when it's supposed to?  An alarm clock ticks throughout the day each time determining if it need to sound the alarm every second that passes.  It will not do it's thing if it's not powered on and EAs are the same way.  The broker does not do the work for you and when you set something like this up the logic behind the EA is not stored someplace magically and continues to run for you even after you close the software.  It requires that everything be in place and running, period.

--- 帖子 #1330 ---
For mike:

This is one of the most valuable system i have tested.

For everyone in this thread:

I have concluded that the system would work more accurate if price is not ranging on larger TF's, hence we have to look at the higher timeframes to make sure that we are in a correct trend.

Always remember that this system only works on trends, NOT SIDEWAYS, because in a sideway condition, price always bounce at support and resistance, before a breakout.

Consequently, always beware when currencies are on sideways on the higher timeframes. To help this, always draw trend lines for the higher TF's.

Just My 2 cents

--- 帖子 #1381 ---
Hi folks.

For all those confused by the new comparative between the D95P and PipNick settings it's really quite simple.

There is no new EA for PipNick's settings. Simply adjust the settings on your existing EA (depending on the broker) to suit the following:

trade time = 8am gmt

look back = 24hrs

sl = move 3rd order to b/e when tp2 hit

This means that in the Fall Version North Finance EA I've made the DayStartHour:10 , the LookBackHours:24 and the UpdateToBE:30 which should (I think) be the same as the settings used by PickNick.

The DayStartHour will vary slightly according to the MT4 broker you use.

If you need to use a timeconverter then do so: http://www.timeanddate.com/worldclock/converter.html

For example, I calculated 8am GMT to equal 6pm Brisbane which is 10hrs difference from when orders are placed by the EA at 8am here in Brisbane. Based on the D95P settings,the DayStartHour on the NF EA is usually set to 0, so I've simply added 10hrs to that to arrive at a setting of 10.

Regarding the upcoming comparative, I'll be using 2 North Finance demo accounts, one with the above PipNick settings and the other with the same D95P settings I've been using practically all along. ie. DayStartHour:0 , LookBackHours: 17 and UpdateToBE: 15

I hope this clarifies things somewhat and I look forward to the comparative.

rgs

mike

I'm affraid it is not exeactly as you posted.

Pipnink wrote: "sl = move 3rd order to b/e when tp2 hit".

If you change UpdateToBE setting on the EA to 30, it means that the 2nd order's SL will not be changed to BE when first TP hit (15). And this is not what Pipnick wrote. He wrote that we need to change ONLY the third order's SL.

--- 帖子 #1390 ---
I am sure you are correct, smilee89. Pipninck trades manually and so can alter the sl in this way. I am fairly sure the ea cannot do this.

--- 帖子 #1406 ---
Hi all. Those who have been following this thread closely will know that I'm yet to commit any live funds to this strategy and as mentioned in post#1 I do not encourage anyone to do so until thorough testing of this system has been done.

I understand that it's sometimes hard to resist the temptation of 'jumping in' and there have been numerous occasions when I've been on the verge of going live myself.

In a recent post I mentioned that I was almost ready to go live, however I've chosen to hold off for another 2-3 weeks until the comparative between the D95P and PipNick settings shows some conclusive results.

One lesson I've learnt from forex trading is that a surefire recipe for failure is to dabble for a short period in any given system, pull out when experiencing some drawdown thus concluding that it's an unprofitable system, and then move onto another system to repeat the same process again. People, you will undoubtedly lose money following this approach.

I consider it a better option to be a little more patient and test a system as thoroughly as possible before being convinced of taking the next step of going live. Even if the live experience is different to the demo trading I'll be rest assured that I allowed sufficient time for testing first.

rgs

mike

--- 帖子 #1409 ---
Time to throw in my two cents worth...

You can back test and forward test in a demo accounts all you want - everything ALWAYS varies when you start putting real money on the line.

Why - because there are just too many variables - the market is ALWAYS changing.  We try to identify and exploit common patterns and characteristics, but nothing is a for sure thing.  It could all change tomorrow.  If you do not understand or are not comfortable with this simple fact, then you are investing in the wrong place.

The broker I use will allows me to enter orders as small as .01 lots.  That is 10 cents per pip on the line or risking 9.00 per day to trade the 3 pairs with the EA live as Mike has laid it out.  Now I realize that every broker will not allow you to enter such small live orders...

- BUT IF THEY DO AND IF YOU ARE NOT TRADING THIS SYSTEM LIVE -

then take my advice and find some system you are willing to risk 9.00 per day on and quit wasting your time on this thread.  There are other systems out there that might better fit your trading style in this forum alone.

Happy New Year - 2008 promises to be a year filled with opportunities to capture as many pips as you can handle.  You just have to find or develop a system that fits your trading style and run with it...

--- 帖子 #1440 ---
Steve and all - for whatever its worth here are my thoughts...

NFP of course means volitility.  From my observations, this often involves a strong move in one direction, followed by retracing back.  Look at EU today - it jumped 100 pips one way and retraced back 40+.  Using this observation, I am trading NFP in this fashion.

1.  If I cannot be at the computer during the announcement, I will just skip this day or close everything before the announcements.

2.  Unless I have a strong feeling on what the initial move is going to be, I close any orders that are open.  If I do have that feeling, then I will close any open orders that contradict that feeling.

3.  For unopened orders, I will monitor those closely and watch for the orders being opened.  When a set of trades are opened, I watch for that intial move to 'stall out' and then I close everything that did not hit the TP as quick as I can.

To answer your question - did you feel the market was going to move in your favor?  If so - then you were prudent - if not - luck.

Me - I was on the sidelines this morning...

Tim

One nasty thing I did forget to add - gaps.  Although it is not too common, with very volitle news event there can be a gap in price.  The market instantly jumps say 100 pips or more.  Since the market never hit your price point, your sl, tp, entry price you entered into the computer cannot be honored.  Instead, you will get the price AFTER the gap.  For example, if you had an open order that was at break even with a 30 pip stop loss and the market jumped 100 pips against you, you would get stopped out at a 100 pip loss, not the 30 pip you anticipated.  Just something to be aware of...

--- 帖子 #1441 ---

Hello at all, specifically at mikelath.

I am a great fan of Daily95pips.

I trade it manually without an ea since november 2007.

Many ideas come around here to optimise the system with different currencys.

I propose the following idea:

Well, we all want trade gbp/jpy currency because there was alot of money to make with

but the volatility was to big so it fails often with d95p parameters.

(Sorry for my english because its not my native language.)

My idea is to trade gbp/jpy with the d95p system and another set of parameters.

I try a lot of parameters in backtesting and i have found

a setting that are best for gbp/jpy but it cannot named daily95pips.

I backtesting manually 'set and forget' that mean i do not move any SL to BE or so

will mean its free to optimse for smaller losses.

Since 19 Nov 2007 i do forwardtesting it as always with good performance.

Here are the settings for gbp/jpy:

Buy/Long Orders:

1 - Entry = HIGH+5pips, Take Profit=40pips, S/L=60pips

2 - Entry = HIGH+5pips, Take Profit=80pips, S/L=60pips

3 - Entry = HIGH+5pips, Take Profit=110pips, S/L=60pips

Vice versa for Short

Time to set Orders is 5pm EST.

High and low of the previous 17hrs.

Need good moneymanagement and something to reserve to overcome negative weeks.

Happy trading and greetigs

Naranjoe

--- 帖子 #1459 ---
Here are the new Experts that I have been working on for the past month for D95P. I have been monitoring the thread and I have taken care of all the problems with the previous EA versions that have been discussed.

These EAs are set up to trade the rules that have been discussed and that are in place currently for D95P. You cannot change any of the inputs at the present time with the exception of the risk % and fixed lots. I have set them for you so that there is no confusion among everyone as to what the settings should be. Just attach them to your charts for the brokers indicated and let them do the work.

If you wish to continue testing with different settings you will need to use one of the older versions at the present time. I currently do not have the time to write a new instruction manual on the settings of the new EAs.

I have rewritten all the code from the previous versions, so these EA versions are a lot more complicated. Take a look in the experts tab in the terminal window and the EAs give you a lot of information as to what is going on.

Look at my following post to find the versions for PipNick.

Have a PipFull Day

--- 帖子 #1475 ---
azjeff,

You can use the EA for Ikon Royal if it is on the same time as FXDD. The only problem may be the trades that are initiated on Sunday/Monday. This depends on when the first bar is formed for the trading day. If they open for trading at the same time FXDD does there will be no problem.

jeta & lukegan,

You can back test strategies all day long, but you will not get accurate stats from the MT4 back-tester. It does not back-test from tick data and that is the only way to get accurate results.

smilee89,

I do not follow the GBP-JPY pair so I am not sure what the High for the 24 hour period was. I can take a look into it if you let me know what broker you are using. The most the EA should move the price from the high or low is 5 pips and that is only if the current price at the time the orders are placed is the same or greater than the high or low for the period.

yen44x,

This would be the correct lot amount for risking 2%, which is the default setting on the EA. If you want to change it you can in the inputs section. You can either change the risk percent or set it to a fixed lot size.

Have A PipFull Day

--- 帖子 #1476 ---
jeta & lukegan,

You can back test strategies all day long, but you will not get accurate stats from the MT4 backtester. It does not backtest from tick data and that is the only way to get accurate results.

Amen

Backtesting in an MT4 environment is the forex equivalent of fool's gold - it looks pretty but has no real value.  If you do not have tick for tick data, it will NEVER be accurate.

Even demo accounts can give you varying results.  Unless someone has a better idea, the only real way I know to test is to set up LIVE accounts, using the smallest lots possible, and monitor the results that way...

--- 帖子 #1486 ---
I am still here.  I took off for the holidays but have started up my testing again at the start of this week.  I have been looking at all the interesting posts and my head is spinning.  I think it's great that so many people are involved and trying new settings and it has started me thinking in some other directions as well.  Up until the holidays my testings has been the following to recap:

3 IBFX and 3 NF demo accounts each running 18 pairs.

Demo set 1: start time of 08 GMT / look back hours of 17 (London open)

Demo set 2: start time of 13 GMT / look back hours of 17 (New York open)

Demo set 3: start time of 22 GMT / look back hours of 17 (5pm eastern, original strategy)

Testing on these 6 demos began on the week ending 11/25/2007 and have continued each week (forward testing) minus the past 2 weeks because of the holidays.  The purpose is to see which time frame performs the best and for which pairs in those time frames.  In addition, it was also to see the difference between IBFX and NF to determine which broker performed better.  At this point I'm not really sure I've fully answered that question as some pairs do better on one broker and others do better on the other.  I was really expecting to see a smaller difference between the two and be able to say the following:

1. X broker is better than Y.

2. These pairs should be run in the 08 GMT time frame.

3. These pairs should be run in the 13 GMT time frame.

4. These pairs should be run in the 22 GMT time frame.

There have been some rough weeks that have passed and none seem to be doing very well at this point although I feel with more time things will become clearer and certain pairs in certain time frames will rise above the others as overall winners.

Also I had made the original modifications to the EA to enable reverse trading.  I have had some assistance with testing but none to the extent that I would have taken it so I'm feeling a little neglecting on my duties in that area.  I wish I could test all the scenarios that are rolling around in my brain but my computer wont handle it all.  I have to assume that if one direction is doing poorly consistently then there is a good chance that reversing the direction could be profitable.  There are some pairs that have just done terrible since I started and these may be big winners in a reverse scenario although I have no concrete evidence to prove that.  It seems that Christancho is testing some pairs with the reverse EA with fair results.

I think what I would like to do is drop the NF demos for a couple of reasons.  I can't see myself at this point dropping my live IBFX account to go with NF.  I'm not sure I trust going with a broker outside of my own country.  I realize they may all be crooked to some extent.  I did see a post recently on this thread about Ikon Royal?  They seem like a possible option since the live and demo accounts were so close and I think they're located in New York?  This is always another layer of complexity when testing anything.  Once you finally go live you don't get the same performance.

I did start my original testing again this week and have added a 7th demo.  This is an IBFX demo account running on 18 pairs with PipNick's settings.

08 start time

24 hour look back

update to be at 30

If I drop the NF demos I will be adding 3 IBFX demos to test the same time frames but with the reverse EA.  It may also be wise to add the other 2 time frames with PipNick's settings.  I'm not sure I could or would want to run 9 demo accounts on my computer at once.

I feel I've rambled enough...

Any thoughts?

--- 帖子 #1520 ---
Naranjoe

The problem with backtesting is that it is not tick for tick - meaning it does not look at what happened during a period of time - only what the opening and close price for that period was.

ie.  For a given period, if the open price was 1.4750  - the high 1.4850, the low 1.4650 and close 1.4750 - a backtest would view that period as if the market did not move.  In real time, using Mike's system, you could have a 90 pip loss <OR> a 95 pip gain and in either case would been closed out for the day.  If backtesting - nothing would have happened or changed.

Now I too am using IBFX, central time zone.  If I understand correctly, to match your settings on the EA, I should be using 22 as the start time with 17 as the number of look back hours.

Thanks

Tim

--- 帖子 #1549 ---
If you like to use EA, you must make sure that you have selected "Allow Live Trading" when installing your EA in your chart. If not, it won't work. Also, you need to activate EA on your account. Make sure you have contacted your broker if you want to trade live using EA. Using demo account, you can use EA to trade but in live account you can't. It must be enabled on broker side.

--- 帖子 #1556 ---
I have three copies of MT4 loaded.  I use different ones for different accounts and a demo account.  During installation just specify a different directory name for the install.  Add a "1" to the end of the directory name, for example.

You can also run multiple instances of the same MT4 program, if you want to.  If the second instance is connected to a different account, you will not see the other account's trades.

I am running on WinXP with no problems.  Had the same arrangement with MT3, too.

-- Gary

--- 帖子 #1579 ---
4thSpace,

The point of an EA is so you don't have to be around.  To answer your question, you setup the EA anytime, tell it when to look back at the hi/lo, leave your computer on with the EA live and let it do its thing. The trick is to leave your computer on, MetaTrader running and connected to your broker when you are not home. The EA will then setup your long and short stop orders at the appropriate time of the day. Hope that helps.

--- 帖子 #1586 ---
The times you need to pay attention to are GMT and the time your broker uses in MetaTrader. When someone mentions setting up trades at a specific time GMT, then you add or subtract from that number based on the time your broker uses.

For example: MikeLath's original posts suggest using the close of the trading day to look back at the previous 17 hours for the high and low. The end of the trading day is 22:00 GMT, 17:00 EST, etc. My broker uses CET, or GMT +1, so my setting should be hour 23, look back 17 hours and cancel order after 24 hours. Hope that helps. Give it some time if you haven't used EA's before.

--- 帖子 #1589 ---
That is correct no orders would execute.

No need to overcome the problem. At the end of the day, the pending orders will be deleted, and the next day High low will start up with a new high and low. So you would have one day that did not execute, but your next day probably will. It has happened to me a couple of times. I have never estimated a High low. I let the EA do all the work.

~ken

I am testing D95p using an external math package. I use 1 minute data (ask/bid) to backtest - ask-hi for buying, bid-lo for selling, s/l and t/p levels (a bit pessimistic, still huge amount of data). Not sure how realistic this is though. I'll post results if someone is interested. Some questions...

- there is a trailing stop version in the code; seems to be a good idea to let profits run in case of a real breakout. Did someone test that?

- There seem to be only compiled versions of the newer EA - is the source code for the current version available somewhere? I am running four currency pairs on a demo account, does not seem to work at the weekend.

- did someone think about volatility based adjustments of the levels (s/l, t/p)? This could be ATR or 17h high/low difference that is calculated anyway. Could make the whole

a bit more robust against market changes?

- If you look at the daily results, some days close with profit and on others, all trades are stopped out with max. loss. In those days, the reverse version would probably work fine. Did someone try to guess whether to take the normal or reverse version that day? I wonder how much better than 50% the accuracy of such a decision needs to be in order to be useful. When training a NN or a support vector machine, at least the question what would be expected as output would be clear (remains the question of input).

--- 帖子 #1628 ---
Great now that we can decide whether to delete the opposite order or not there are other things that should be concidered and I think are possible to make this work better.

Again I have traded these markets for the past tow years and have made consistent profits using the following system that should be easy to incorporoate in this EA. Keep in mind that some Majot traders use this system as well. I cannot speak to who they are but they are Major traders.

The rules they put down are quite simple Trades are made between Midnight EST and 3: am EST playing against the volatitity of the market at that time. Keep in mind also that since no news reports are released at these times the pips spread remains fairly stable. Trades ar eonly placed f the consolidation high to low is less than 80 pips apart. If so then the straddle is placed 20 pips above and below with a stoploss of 40 pips and a limit order of 40 pips. They trade the GBP/USD and the EUR/JPY.

The current EA placed three trades and will work fine but if it could read back and see if the consolidation is within the 80 pips and then placed the trades and if not within the 80 pips then place no trades this would eliminate some bad trades as we now see them.

I am sure that the EA could be adjusted to do this as it now looks back 17 or 24 hours then places the trades then it should be able to do the same , see if we are within the 80 pis and then make a decision to trade or not.

THere is another profitable system to this as well bu lets see if we can attack this problem first.

Also I have seen throughout his forum that we are trading the near NY open when the better time is the European open between Midnight EST and 3: am EST

Bernard

The rules they put down are quite simple Trades are made between Midnight EST and 3: am EST playing against the volatitity of the market at that time.

Taking this into concideration we are looking back 5 hours from midnight EST for any movement within the 80 pis range. If there is nothing more than 80 pips then we make the trades.

I have attached an indicator that show this quite well. I trade off it manually all the time using this system.If we could make an EA from this indicator it would be great as well.

--- 帖子 #1643 ---
Hi Mike,

Try this idea for your Daily 95.  Make your 15pip profit trade with 3x lots, the 30 trade with 2x lots, and the 50 trade with 1x lot.

For example,

Make first trade at Buy with a take profit of +15    --- lot size = .03  (or 3)

Make first trade at Buy with a take profit of +30    --- lot size = .02  (or 2)

Make first trade at Buy with a take profit of +50    --- lot size = .01  (or 1)

The idea here is that hitting the nearby targets is more likely than hitting the far targets therefore bet heavier on the nearby target.  AND if the first target is hit, but not targets 2 & 3 you will cover your losses better when stopped out.

Give it a try and let me know what you think.

Good trading on you,

Tom Trader

--- 帖子 #1646 ---
Hi all,

I was thinking in the same direction than Tom here. I've been forward testing Naranjoe's settings with GBP/JPY and Mike's for GBP/USD for the last couple of weeks. I know 2 weeks is not an acceptable sample size, but only in 2 days (out of 14) the first profit target wasn't hit after the trades were triggered, while several times the market decided to turn the other way after the 1st TP was reached, resulting in an overall loss. It isn't necessarily true that this way, when no TP is hit, the losses would be higher. That is just a matter of money management. You have to play with your lot sizes according to your loss tolerance. I think this approach is worth a try, at least.

My $0.02

Ariel

take the calculation again by using the same amount of lots but split them up differently.

According to Tom:

Same Basis: 3 Lots.

3/6= 0,5

3*0,5= 1,5 Lot on the 15P Target

2*0,5=1 Lot on the 30P Target

1*0,5= 0,5 Lots on the 50P Target.

You will see that the results will differ from yours.

--- 帖子 #1655 ---
Naranjoe, sorry for the misunderstanding...

You are indeed increasing your size lot, doubling each trade's size. This way, your risk also doubles, but we should keep the same money management, i.e. the same maximum loss. By doubling your size lots, you are in fact risking twice the money than before, and I think that was what Bennyfx was referring to.

Tom Trader increased the lot sizes indeed, but if you want to compare results with your original settings, you should maintain the same overall amount of money you put in the trades.

Hope I'm clear enough (it's late here and I've been the whole day working on the PC, so my brain is a little blurred).

Well, good night to you all.

Middleastern

--- 帖子 #1656 ---
I think you fool yourself with this results. (No offence)

But the answer is given by yourself:  "I increase the lot amount as it has described by TomTrader."

So you doubled your input.

--> More input = More output

This is why every result is exactly twice as high in $$$.

--- 帖子 #1662 ---
I have only read the post partially, but I think we can find a way to adapt the daily95 method in order to work. I am currently backtesting some alternatives and I think the problem stays this way:

- it only applies to pairs that are prone to "explode" (run stops, spike higher/lower, etc...) and that is GBP/JPY especially but EUR/NZD also. The spread on these pairs is 7.

- if some broker can offer us a spread of 7 for TRY or other very illiquid pair, please post it here so I can do some checking. Thank you

- from a logical point of view, we are just following the trend; what is illogical is risking 90 pips for 95, so I am currently backtesting only the 30 pips for 50 alternative

- we are looking for volatility in order to have fast moves covering a lot of ground, so it would be interesting to use a volatility indicator such as ATR or Bollinger Bands (if the price action closes outside the upper/lower BB it might be a sign of increased volatility in the next period). Options pricing in GBP/JPY might give us a clue of where the volatility stands at a given moment, but I have limited experience with options and maybe someone else here knows more.

- we also want to avoid the ranging days (which appear quite often in gbp/jpy as a matter of fact), so it would be interesting to compare the system 1) in days with market-moving news releases (like interest rate statement in GBP) and 2) in days with no news or limited importance news.

I think that in the end we will have a system, but not an automatic system because we will gauge in some factors that depend on our appreciation. Please tell me what you think.

--- 帖子 #1681 ---
Discussions are welcome.  Hey, firstly, i hate to talk in mathematics. so just try to be plain. it's like this:

i think that this system, is a random luck system.  using previous day's HH to buy, is not really indicating that we are following bull.  neither is previous LL.

no matter what direction u go, and no matter what level u go from, it is a matter of random luck in long term.  check those candles, two consecutive bearish candle, but u still can possibly win profit, if u buy from previous HH.  it happens frequently.

we are not doing a trend following system, since this is a one-day trading system.  if we talk about trend-following or contrarian, we may be joking.

now, why 15 TP with 30 SL is better than 30 TP with 30 SL, in my humble opinion, is because, generally, more than 50% likely, it is easier to reach 15 than 30.  forget about directions, imagine u ask John and Tom, two random men, everyday, u command: run! John and Tom.  Since John's task is 15 feet, and Tom's goal is 30 feet,  after many many years, who won most by finishing his job earlier everyday? It should be John.

when consider profit/loss ratio, probability must be involved.  we cannot say that 30 SL vs 15 TP is like 2:1 risk/return ratio.  That's wrong, because we didn't consider probability.

Again, since i said price not moving in straightline, it is of coz frequently seen like eur/jpy profit in both ways.

thanks, i like discussions, please.

Dear Middleastern

You may have hit the jackpot here.  Based upon your data on the GBP/JPY pair, you say you are hitting the TP=25 approximately 80% of the time.  If you have a system that has an 80% win/loss ratio then you have a real money maker.

Where do you have your stop loss set at?  If it is at 25, then your score should look something like this:

2 losses @ 25 pips = 50 pip loss

8 wins   @ 25 pips = 400 pip wins

-------------------------------------

Net gain = 350 pips  (GREAT!!!)

--- 帖子 #1695 ---
Hi Tom,

SL was as Naranjoe's settings = 60 pips. As you see, the risk/reward ratio is 60:25, which is not the best, but if the win/lose ratio is around 80%, I guess it is compensated.

HOWEVER, I just tested it on 28 days, which is in no way whatsoever a significant sample, statistically speaking. I'll check the previous months on GBP/JPY, and as soon as I have some results I'll post them.

It would be great if someone could do the same with another pair, to have a more robust base.

Another thing to have in mind is that betting only on the smaller TP's will keep us out of the big rides. There is a trade off here, higher win/lose ratios in exchange of the big trends. We will always be able to put bigger lot sizes to overcome this, provided that the win/lose ratio consistenly stays at those levels, what has yet to be proved...

Regards

Middleastern

--- 帖子 #1703 ---
Hello Tom and everyone out there,

I apologize if this is a little bit off-topic, but I think it is interesting. I've back-tested two pairs, from Aug 1, 2007 to Feb 15, 2008 (Broker = Alpari. Trading days: Monday to Friday only) using smaller TP's. Here are the results:

EUR/GBP

SL = 30; TP's = 15, 20 & 30

Orders placed at 08 am GMT. Look back hours = 16. Buy stops at High+5; Sell stops at Low-5. The backtesting was done manually on the 1H chart.

.................TP

............15        ...20            ...30

..........n    %    ..n    %      ..n    %

[+]            ...91  74   77  63    68  55

[-]            ...32  26   46  37    55   45

Total days tested = 139. Total no-touch days = 16 (No-touch days were not considered to calculate the percentages)

GBP/JPY

SL = 50; TP's = 30, 40 & 50

Orders placed at 08 am GMT. Look back hours = 16. Buy stops at High+5; Sell stops at Low-5. The backtesting was done manually on the 1H chart.

................TP

..........30        ....40             ....50

.........n   %       ...n   %          ..n   %

[+]   ...99  75   91  69     85  64

[-]          ...33  25   41  31     47  36

Total days tested = 139. Total no-touch days = 7 (No-touch days were not considered to calculate the percentages)

Comments:

On the EUR/GBP I considered positive days also those that had a positive result at 8 am GMT of the next day, but their TP was not yet hit (and there were many of those). For a qualitative test, I think this does.

This pair has a very low daily range (mean = 43 pips in the last 180 days), and that's why I took it - a pair with a behavior opposite to that of GBP/JPY.

On GBP/JPY, the TP's were always hit. Something I noticed (and for many of you I'm sure this is not news), is that this pair jumps quite a bit on the early hours of the London session. I chose 8 am GMT to place the orders because of my time zone (GMT+2), and it turned out to be a good choice, it seems. On this pair, it may be a good idea to use a small trailing stop instead of a TP in order to lock  profits and enjoy some of the eventual big moves.

I think the direction to follow on this approach is to define the TP's based on the average daily ranges of each pair during the last 2 weeks/3 weeks/month (?), to optimize them. It would require a re-check of the daily ranges every two weeks or so to adapt the TP's to the current behavior of each specific pair - If it was trending in the last weeks, expand the TP's. If it was ranging, reduce them.

Well, some food for thought. Comments and suggestions are expected.

Middleastern

Attempts to isolate errors.

1. Download the Daily 95 Pips (IBFX Fall Ver..mq4 from the attachment Page.

2. Start MT4 without any EA's attached.

3. Attach D95P EA only to one chart (for example EUR/USD).

4. Check inputs of the EA (for test purpose set the DayStartHour to the next full hour of your Broker)

Wait and see if something happens when the hour has begun.

See in the Journal tab of MT4 if there are errormessages.

If it still does not work, please report again.

Naranjoe

--- 帖子 #1777 ---
Some thoughts and results for those interested.

I have been manually testing the following system for a few months:-

Pairs: GBP/USD & EUR/JPY

Start Time: 8am GMT

Look back: 24hrs

Pip Targets: 15, 30, 50

S/L: 30 pips

Change order to B/E: 30 pips

Apart from the start time and lookback, this system is essentially as Mike's original on page 1.

The attached spreadsheet has the following worksheets

Trades - Details of each every trade

Daily Summary - Results for each day

Analysis - Results for each pair broken down by pip target (inspired by mtaboneweb's recent post).

The system started very well before xmas but then struggled early in the year. It has since picked up again and for the 2 pairs has yielded 1334 pips for 63 trading days (avg 21.17 per day) - not bad at all.

However, from the analysis you will see the 30 pip profit target is barely profitable. The 15 pip target is most profitable. Over the same period the system would have yielded 2205 pips if the 3 orders were all placed with a 15 pip target.

To state the obvious, a high probablity strategy can negate the need for a high reward to risk ratio. although I acknowledge this strategy has only been tested over a very short period of time.

Naranjoe - if possible I would be interested to see similar analysis for gbp/jpy if you have the data.

Be interested in anyone elses thoughts on this.

Cheers

Nick

Edit - Spreadsheet is too big - Analysis tab only attached

Hi

I check the following

for GBP/USD

Buy: Make first   Buy at
(last day high) + 5 pips
with a take profit of +15 --- lot size = .02 (or 2)

Buy:Make second Buy  at
(last day high) + 25 pips
with a take profit of +15 --- lot size = .01 (or 1)

(the same for Sell)

------------

in that way you will close the first position and only after it continue another 5 pips (you get a confirmation), you will open a new position

-----------

I make 357.6pips in the last 11 days approx.

------------

please check it, and let me know what do you think and if i need to change add something...

Martin:

The E/U does perform very well with this method.  I backtested a system where I entered at 5 pips above/below for the E/U, G/U and entered at 11% ATR(14) above/below for G/J, E/J. --- 帖子 #1811 ---
Unicla:

My entry for the G/J, E/J was not 5 pips off hi/lo but rather 11% ATR(14) off hi/lo.  G/J is very volatile, so the ATR is usually 200-300 pips per day.  I would take 11% of the ATR(14), add that to the hi, subtract from the low for my entry to ensure a true breakout.  For example, G/J ATR(14) is 2.50, so I would enter the market 28 pips above the high, below the low for the day.

Here were my settings for each of the four pairs:

E/U:  enter at 5, TP at 15, 30, 50, SL at 25 (trailing stop on 3rd order)

G/U:  enter at 5, TP at 15, 30, 50, SL at 30 (trailing stop on 3rd order)

E/J:  enter at 11% ATR(14), TP at 15%, 30%, 55% ATR(14), SL at 60 (trailing stop on 3rd order)

G/J:  enter at 11% ATR(14), TP at 15%, 30%, 55% ATR(14), SL at 75 (trailing stop on 3rd order)

Bioquim

--- 帖子 #1812 ---
Do you mean ATR of 14 1h bars? This would be just looking one day back. Or do you use 14 days? This might be more stable.

Anyway the question is how the parameters could be adjusted depending on market conditions. ATR certainly seems to be a good idea to cope with different volatilities. Another possibility would be to periodically optimize the parameters for optimum result (using a robust measure). For example you could run an optimization each weekend, finding optimal settings based on the data for the last four weeks and use this setting for the next week.

Ideally we would also know when to apply our system... it works best on a trending market, I think. If there is little movement within a small range, we lose mostly.

--- 帖子 #1813 ---

--- 帖子 #1845 ---
The settings highly influence the success of this strategy. I have only tried the E/U and the G/J. The E/U works good with the classic setting of 15/30/50 and SL 30 and BE 15. Perhaps it works better with other settings, but these work ok.

The G/J works best for me if the classic settings are doubled. That means 30/60/100 (or TS on the last order), SL 60, and BE 25 (or perhaps 30). I have seen that others use a BE of 55-60.

Good luck with the trading!

--- 帖子 #1876 ---
periodBegin and periodEnd define the "outlined box" inside the box (this is the period in which the indicator adjusts high and low as it changes, it doesn't count the first candle though).

BoxEnd is up to when you want the overall box (outlined part and non-outlined) to be shown on your chart.

All times should be referred to your own platform time and not local time.

--- 帖子 #1897 ---
So it looks like you guys are trying to develop/optimize something a strategy based on opening range breakout theory.  These are used by professional traders all the time, as they give you a considerable edge, but they almost all experience sharp drawdowns you have to trade through.

The only thing I'm curious about is why do you leave all 6 orders running?  Usually ORB strategies implement orders OCO (One-Cancels-the-Other).  Example, if your long orders got triggered, your shorts would be done for the day, and vice versa.  This removes the chance of the double k.o. when you have big losses in each direction.

Also, I'm joining the thread kind of late, and I noticed that there are 181 attachments.  Which is the latest version and is pipnick still using his?
